Comprehensive Collection of Ancient and Modern Books, Medical Section, Volume 153

Lips and Mouth

Huangdi’s Suwen

Treatise on the True Words of the Golden Coffer

The center is yellow, connected to the spleen, opening at the mouth, and storing essence in the spleen. [Note: The center is the position of earth, the spleen is the earth organ, and its qi is interconnected. Yellow is the color of earth, and the mouth is the orifice of the spleen.]

Discussion on the Correspondence of Yin and Yang

The center generates dampness, dampness produces earth, earth generates sweetness, sweetness nourishes the spleen, the spleen generates flesh, flesh generates the lungs, and the spleen connects to the mouth, which is the orifice. [Note: The qi of the spleen is connected to the mouth, and when the spleen is harmonious, it can discern the flavors of grains, hence the spleen governs the mouth. The spleen serves to welcome nourishment, which is why its orifice is at the mouth.]

Discussion on the Six Energetic Organs

The spleen, stomach, large intestine, small intestine, three burners, and bladder are the foundation of the granary and the residence of nourishment, referred to as vessels. Their manifestation can be seen in the white flesh of the four corners of the lips. [Note: The spleen receives food and water as a transport official, the intestines receive and transmit food and water, the three burners regulate the water pathways, the bladder is the organ of water essence, thus they are the foundation of the granary. The spleen houses nourishment, thus it is called the residence of nourishment. The spleen possesses the qi of raising, lowering, entering, and exiting, hence it is termed a vessel. The four whites refer to the white flesh at the four edges of the lips. The mouth is the orifice of the spleen and governs the flesh, hence the manifestation is found in the white flesh of the lips.][1p]

Discussion on Diagnosis

The Yangming channel indicates the end, with movements of the mouth and eyes, leading to excessive surprise and vain talk, and a yellow complexion. If there is a lack of benevolence above and below, it is the end.

Discussion on Heat

In five days, the Shaoyin suffers. The Shaoyin pulse connects to the kidney, branches to the lung, and is linked at the base of the tongue, causing dryness in the mouth and tongue and thirst. On the eleventh day, the Shaoyin disease weakens, thirst ceases, there is no fullness, and the tongue is dry followed by sneezing.

The six energies interact; though they enter into the yin within, they all manifest as heat symptoms, hence the dryness and thirst. As the pathogenic qi gradually weakens, the righteous qi begins to recover, thus thirst ceases. Those affected by cold on both sides suffer; if it lasts one day, both the Juyin and Shaoyin are affected, resulting in headaches, dry mouth, and fullness.

This also discusses the dual effects of yin and yang in disease. The Taiyang and Shaoyin interact as exterior and interior; if both are afflicted simultaneously, it results in Taiyang headaches and Shaoyin's fullness and dry mouth.

Discussion on Qi Blocking

Heat from the bladder moves to the small intestine, causing hindered bowel movements, resulting in oral ulcers.

The pulse of the small intestine connects to the heart, following the throat down to the bladder, as it pertains to the small intestine. The lower part of the small intestine is called the “gate of the ileum,” which separates and filters fluids, seeping into the bladder. Heat transferred back from the bladder to the small intestine causes the intestines to fail to descend. The damp heat qi adversely reverses along the channel, leading to ulceration of the mouth.[2p]

Discussion on Wind

The injuries caused by wind, particularly in summer, lead to what is called "heart wind." The symptoms of heart wind include excessive sweating, aversion to wind, dryness and burning sensations, propensity for anger and fright, and a red complexion. In severe cases, speech becomes difficult. Diagnosis reveals a red color in the mouth. [Note: The heart is associated with the fire organ; when wind is excessive, fire becomes intense, resulting in dry and cracked lips with a deficiency of moisture. Wind transforms wood, and the conflict of wood and fire leads to easy anger and fear. The heart governs the tongue; if the condition worsens, the tongue becomes strong but speech becomes difficult. When the heart is harmonious, the tongue can discern the five flavors, hence the diagnosis involves the mouth.]

When wind enters the interior for a long time, it causes intestinal wind leading to diarrhea. If it affects the skin's surface, it results in "leakage wind." The symptoms of leakage wind include heavy sweating, with sweat soaking through clothing, and dryness in the mouth. When the wind pools above, it impedes effort, and if the body is in pain, it is accompanied by coldness. [Note: The qi of the spleen and stomach governs the muscles externally and the abdomen internally. If the wind pathogen remains in the muscles and enters the interior, it injures the qi of the spleen and stomach, resulting in intestinal wind and diarrhea. The large and small intestines both belong to the stomach. If it remains long in the exterior muscles, the yang qi disperses outward, leading to leakage wind. Leakage wind occurs when the skin opens and the qi is harmed, which causes excessive sweating. Sweat leaking onto clothing gradually soaks through, signifying that the source is not closed. The loss of fluids leads to dryness in the mouth. When the wind accumulates above, affecting the upper body, the interplay of wind and dampness harms the yang qi, leading to inability to exert oneself. If one tends to labor excessively, the body will be in pain and feel cold.][3p]
Discussion on Atrophy

When the liver qi is hot, it leads to bile leakage, a bitter mouth, and dryness in the sinews and membranes. When the sinews and membranes are dry, the muscles become tense and spasm, resulting in muscular atrophy. [Note: The gallbladder is an organ that stores essence and corresponds to the sinews. The sinews throughout the body are nourished by the essence contained in the gallbladder. When the gallbladder is attached to the liver, if the liver qi is hot, bile leaks out causing a bitter mouth; when bile leaks, the sinews and membranes lack nourishment and become dry, leading to tension and spasm that result in atrophy.]

Discussion on Syncope

When there is syncope in the lesser yin, it results in dry mouth, red urine, abdominal distension, and heart pain. [Note: The foot lesser yin pulse belongs to the kidneys, connects with the bladder, passes through the liver diaphragm, enters the lungs, exits to connect with the heart, travels through the throat, and underlies the root of the tongue. When the meridians are reversed, the yin fluids cannot ascend, hence the dry mouth and heart pain. The lung metal cannot regulate the lower part, leading to red urine. When the energies of water and fire, yin and yang do not interact, it results in abdominal distension.]

Discussion on Rare Diseases[4p]
The Emperor said: What is the name of the disease that causes a sweet taste in the mouth? How does one acquire it? Qi Bo replied: This is the overflow of the five qi, called spleen dampness. The five flavors enter through the mouth, stored in the stomach, and the spleen regulates their essence and energy. The fluid in the spleen causes the mouth to taste sweet. This is produced by rich and fatty foods. Such a person must often consume sweet and rich food, which leads to internal heat, and the sweetness causes fullness, resulting in an overflow of qi that transforms into thirst. Treat it with orchids to eliminate the accumulated old qi.

[Note: The five qi refers to earth qi, which is central; in number it is five, in flavor it is sweet, in odor it is fragrant, in organ it is the spleen, and in orifice it is the mouth. Eating too much sweet and rich food leaves foul odors in the spleen, causing the spleen qi to overflow and manifest externally. Rich flavors generate internal heat, and sweetness tends to linger. The spleen is responsible for transporting fluid from the stomach. When the five flavors are consumed, the fluids each follow their path; sweetness reaches the spleen first, and consuming rich sweet food often leads to internal heat retention. Fluids cannot be distributed among the five organs and remain isolated in the spleen. When spleen qi overflows, it causes the mouth to taste sweet. Treat it with orchids to eliminate the accumulated old qi.]

The Great Treatise on Qi Transformation

In a year of inadequate metal, the fire of inflammation predominates, causing people to suffer from mouth sores, and in severe cases, heart pain.

[Note: In the year of the sixth yi, when metal energy fails, the conquering fire energy prevails. With weak metal and excessive fire, water then restores balance. The cold water qi ascends, pressing on the heart's fire, leading to mouth sores and severe heart pain among the people.][5p]
The Great Discussion on the Five Constants and Governance

The chronicle of preparation for transformation is centered around the mouth.
(Note: Preparation for transformation refers to the earth's governance; earth corresponds to the spleen, and the spleen opens to the mouth.) The wind of the extreme yin descends from the heavens; the energy of the spleen rises, as the earth flourishes and yellow sprouts. When water becomes obstructed, the earth must undergo transformation, experiencing heaviness while the muscles atrophy and the appetite diminishes, leading to a dry mouth.
(Note: The chronicle of earth concerns matters related to earth itself, its organ is the spleen, and its color is yellow. The flourishing earth indicates that the earth's essence is abundant below. The yellow sprouting refers to the earth’s energy rising to the heavens. Since earth transforms under the influence of wood, it is subjected to its overcoming power, resulting in the earth changing and causing spleen ailments characterized by heaviness and decreased appetite.)

The Essential Discussion on Ultimate Truth

The return of the lesser yang indicates that great heat is approaching; the fire energy surges within, causing lesions in the mouth.
(Note: This so-called fire refers to the fire of the lesser yin. When fire energy rises within the upper burner, it results in lesions in the mouth.)

The Classic of the Spiritual Axis

The Chapter on the Forms of Disease in the Organs Caused by Pathogenic Factors

Those with gallbladder ailments tend to sigh heavily; they have a bitter taste in the mouth, vomit undigested bile, experience a faint sensation in the heart area, and fear being captured, with a "heaving" sensation in the throat leading to frequent spitting.
(Note: For those with gallbladder ailments, the gallbladder energy does not rise, hence they sigh to release it. The bitter taste and vomited bile indicate the presence of bile. The faint sensation in the heart area means the gallbladder energy is deficient. The heaving in the throat and frequent spitting indicate a disease in the lesser yang channel.)[6p]
The main channel of the Large Intestine (Hand Yangming) exits at the corner of the mouth and intersects at the Ren Zhong point. It governs diseases arising from bodily fluids, which include yellowing of the eyes, dryness of the mouth, nasal bleeding, throat obstruction, and pain in the shoulder and upper arm.

(Note: The Large Intestine transmits food and water, transforming it into refined essence. Hence, it governs bodily fluids; when there is a deficiency of fluids and an excess of heat, symptoms such as yellowing of the eyes and dryness of the mouth occur.)

The main channel of the Stomach (Foot Yangming) exits at the corner of the mouth, encircles the lips, and connects to the Cheng Jiang point. It governs diseases arising from blood, which include mania, intermittent fevers, excessive sweating, nasal bleeding, crooked mouth, and swollen lips.

(Note: The Stomach is the sea of food and drink and governs the generation of nutritive blood. Therefore, it governs blood-related diseases, leading to conditions like mania and intermittent fever with sweating due to the heat of stomach qi evaporating fluids. Nasal bleeding is due to the heat in the meridians. Crooked mouth and swollen lips indicate diseases of the Yangming channel.)

If the Qi of the Foot Taiyin is exhausted, the pulse will not nourish the muscles. The shoulder and tongue are foundational to the muscles. If the pulse does not nourish, the muscles will be weak; if the muscles are weak, they will atrophy, leading to fullness in the Ren Zhong point. If the Ren Zhong point is full, the lips will invert; if the lips invert, it means the flesh has begun to perish. If the first of the wood element (Yin) is strong and the second of the earth element (Yang) is weak, wood prevails over earth.

(Note: The Qi of the Foot Taiyin originates in the Spleen. The Spleen stores the nourishing essence and externally governs muscle. Thus, if the Taiyin Qi is exhausted, the pulse will not nourish the muscles. The Spleen opens to the mouth and governs the reception of food, making the lips and tongue fundamental to muscle. If the pulse does not nourish, the tongue will wither and the lips will invert, indicating that the vital substance of Taiyin has exhausted externally. If the first of wood is strong and the second of earth is weak, then the Qi of the Spleen dies internally.)[7p]
Chapter on the Meridians of Water

The Yangming of the Foot is straight, following the throat and emerging from the mouth, reaching the forehead and skull.

Chapter on the Tendons

The tendon of the Foot Yangming is positioned above the mouth; its sickness affects the mouth. When the Yangming of the Foot and the Taiyang of the Hand are tense, both the mouth and eyes are affected. [Note: The tendon of the Foot Yangming above the mouth corresponds to the area beneath the eyes. The tendon of the Hand Taiyang is connected to the lower jaw and outer canthus. Thus, if the left tendon is tense, it affects the left side, and one should puncture the left; if the right tendon is tense, it affects the right side, and one should puncture the right.]

Chapter on Cold and Heat Diseases

When the muscles are cold or hot, they ache, hair becomes scorched, and the lips become dry and waxy. [Note: The blood and qi outside the pulse fill the skin and hot flesh, leading to hair growth. Therefore, when the disease affects the muscles, they ache, and hair becomes scorched. The spleen governs the muscles, opening at the mouth, hence the lips become dry and waxy.]

Chapter on Transmission from Teachers

The spleen governs the defenses, directing them to confront food, observing the condition of the lips and tongue to discern auspiciousness or inauspiciousness. [Note: The spleen is the official of transport and circulation, hence governs defenses. Auspiciousness and inauspiciousness depend on the health of the organs—when they are well, it is auspicious; when they are ill, it is inauspicious.] Those with thick lips and a long philtrum indicate the condition of the small intestine. [Note: The mouth is the orifice of the spleen; the small intestine receives the turbid matter from the spleen and stomach and connects to the stomach, thus the lips and philtrum indicate the condition of the small intestine.][8p]
Treatise on Excess and Deficiency in Body Types

In the case of the robust and strong, with ample blood and vitality, firm skin, if they are subjected to malefic influences, the needles penetrate deeply and leave a lasting mark, this is a plump person. They have broad shoulders and thick skin that is dark, with thin flesh around the neck. Their lips are slightly protruding, their blood is dark and turbid, their energy is sluggish and delayed, and in character, they are greedy for gain and contributions. When needles penetrate deeply and remain, it increases their quantity.

[Note: This describes the excess of physical form. Broad shoulders indicate a wide expansion to all sides. The neck represents the domain of the sun; thin flesh and thick, dark skin show the prominence of the sun’s water energy. The lips are an outer indication of the spleen’s earth elements, slightly protruding show the richness of earth energy. The dark coloration represents water’s essence; turbid blood signifies heavy and cloudy vital essence. Sluggish energy indicates thick flesh and obstructed energy pathways. Those who have excess can share, while those who have deficiency are greedy. Both greedy for gain, they fail to achieve the way of balance.

In contrast, lean individuals have thin skin and lack of color, their flesh is light and delicate, their lips are thin and their speech is light. Their blood is clear, their energy is clean, they easily lose vitality, and their blood is vulnerable. Needles should penetrate shallowly and quickly for them.

[Note: This discusses the deficiency in physical form. Thin skin and lack of color signify insufficient atmospheric energy. Light and delicate appearance reflects deficiency in earthly energy. Clear blood indicates lightness and shallow water. Clear energy shows thin muscles and smooth energy pathways.][9p]

The Chapter on the Organs

Those with thin lips have a high spleen, while those with thick lips have a low spleen; strong lips indicate a strong spleen, while large but soft lips indicate a fragile spleen; well-proportioned lips indicate a proper spleen, while uneven lips suggest a tilted spleen.

The Chapter on Abnormal Defensive Qi

Lips that are blue, yellow, red, white, or black indicate illness in the muscles. (Note: Muscles are external to the spleen, and the earth nourishes the four organs; hence, by observing the lip colors - blue, yellow, red, white, and black - one understands that the illness of the defensive qi resides in the muscles.)

The Chapter on Yin and Yang: Twenty-Five Types of People

When there is a deficiency of blood and qi above the foot yangming, both lips may appear thin and drawn. (Note: A deficiency of blood and qi cannot nourish the skin, leading to a lack of fullness. Thus, the thinning of both lips is evident.)[10p]
The Inexpressible Worries and Angers Poem

The lips are the fan of sound.

The Heat Illness Poem

In the case of heat illness lasting seven or eight days, if the pulse is weak and small, the patient shows blood in urine and dryness in the mouth. They may die in a day and a half; if the pulse is absent, death occurs in a day.

Note: Additionally, if the heat does not resolve and it transmits to the lesser yin, it becomes a sign of death. The six meridians circulate; if the illness recurs on the seventh day and does not resolve by the eighth, it is termed a relapse. A weak pulse indicates the lesser yin meridian. The superior to the lesser yin is governed by the sovereign fire. The presence of blood in urine indicates a disease of the lesser yin's water organ. Dryness in the mouth indicates an issue with the hand's lesser yin sovereign fire. A person who dies after a day and a half has succumbed within one or two days, marking the end of the interplay of yin and yang water and fire. The pulse originates in the kidney and is governed by the heart; if the pulse is absent, it signifies a cessation below, resulting in death within a day.

Heat illness may not reveal where it hurts; the patient may suffer from deafness and cannot recover, with dryness in the mouth. If yang heat is severe while yin has considerable cold, heat resides in the marrow—death is beyond remedy.

Note: If the pain of heat illness cannot be located, it indicates external heat has penetrated within. Deafness from inability to recover and dryness in the mouth indicates that kidney heat has risen. Severe yang heat combined with considerable yin cold signifies a struggle between internal heat and external factors. Heat in the marrow indicates internal struggles with external heat. All of these signify a disease that has penetrated deeply within, hence death.[11p]
The Five Readings and Five Uses

The mouth and lips are the organs of the spleen.
(Note: The spleen opens to the mouth, thus the mouth is regarded as the organ of the spleen.)

The Stomach and Intestines

The mouth is two and a half inches wide.

The Mouth Inquiry

When the Yangming qi arrives, one may bite their lips.
(Note: The Yangming meridian encircles the mouth and lips, and when the vital energy reverses upwards, one may bite their lips.)

Discussion on Distention

When there is distention in the gallbladder, there is pain and distention under the ribs, bitterness in the mouth, and one tends to sigh frequently.
(From the "Inner Canon" by Hua Tuo of the Han Dynasty)[12p]

Diagnosis of Diseases

Cold-induced fevers, when the mouth resembles a fish's mouth and cannot close, if there is excessive exhalation and no inhalation, it is fatal. If the patient's mouth is open, they will die within three days.
(From "Essentials of the Gold Coffer" by Zhang Ji, Han Dynasty)

Dry Mouth

In cases of lung wind, the mouth is dry and wheezing occurs, the body feels heavy and swollen. If the abdomen is full and the mouth and tongue are dry, there is water and gas in the intestines; use Jiāo Lì Huáng Yuán as treatment. If there is thirst for water, dry mouth and tongue, prescribe Bai Hu Jia Ren Shen Tang. In cases of jaundice, with fever, irritability, and chest fullness, dry mouth occurs due to fire damaging the sweat during the onset of the disease, resulting in heat. However, jaundice acquired from dampness leads to full-body heating with a yellow face and fever in the abdomen, the heat is interior, and purging is necessary. If the patient experiences fullness in the chest, with parched lips and a bluish tongue, a dry mouth desiring rinse rather than swallowing, without signs of cold or heat, with a slow and weak pulse, and the abdomen is not full, the patient may complain of fullness due to stagnant blood. If the patient exhibits feverish symptoms, fullness, dry mouth and thirst, yet the pulse shows no heat, this indicates hidden yin, which is stagnant blood and should be purged.
(From "Pulse Techniques" by Wang Shuhe, Jin Dynasty)

Diagnostic Methods

Left cun pulse is rapid and forceful, indicating heart heat with a bitter mouth. Right cun pulse is floating and rapid, indicating lung heat with a spicy mouth. Left guan pulse is string-like and rapid, suggesting gallbladder deficiency with a bitter mouth; if it is strong, then liver heat with a sour mouth. Right guan pulse that is sinking and solid indicates spleen heat with a sweet mouth; if rapid, it suggests oral ulcers.[13p]
Canker Lips

Canker lips refer to a condition that occurs on the lips, resembling a silkworm cocoon, hence the name. The Inner Canon states: "The spleen's energy opens at the mouth," and it also says: "The spleen's nourishment resides in the lips." However, dryness leads to cracking, heat causes splits, wind results in tremors, and cold may cause peeling. If there is swelling with a white skin that wrinkles and cracks like a cocoon, it is thus named canker lips. It often begins as a small lump, approximately the size of a bean; or it may regenerate, gradually swelling into a larger mass of about an inch thick; or it may develop into various forms like flowers, waxberries, lumps, lingzhi mushrooms, or fungi, with no fixed shape, all arising from the interaction of the six external pathogens and seven emotions. If one's anxieties and worries are excessive, heart fire can become intense, affecting the spleen channel; or consuming rich wine and heavy flavors can accumulate heat, harming the spleen, leading to the depletion of kidney water. One must carefully assess the causes of the symptoms. Only by replenishing kidney water and nourishing spleen blood will the dryness become moist, the fire diminish, the wind cease, and the swelling resolve. This is a distinct condition, seldom seen, and hard to recognize. If it does not heal after a long time, urgently use heated metal to cauterize it in moxa flames, and internally take the Gui Pi Tang to nourish and restore. This may facilitate healing. However, if one uses external methods to aggressively dissolve the toxins, it may lead to further harm; caution is important! If a woman suffers from this, it is due to a deficiency of Yin blood. It is advisable to treat it with the Si Wu Xiao Yao San.[14p]
On Guidance
Qian Yi, Song Dynasty

Diagnosis of Illness

If the spleen and lungs are ill for a long time, they become deficient, leading to pale lips. The spleen is the mother of the lungs; both being deficient cannot nourish each other, hence the term "timid." The lungs govern the lips; lips that are pale and lustrous indicate good health, while those that are white like withered bones indicate death. If the blood and qi are deficient and timid, and cold invades, the lips may appear blue; a dark forehead and blue lips indicate coldness.

Direct Guidance of Benevolent Study
Yang Shiying, Song Dynasty

Swollen Lips and Mouth Sores

For swollen lips, it is advisable to use Stomach-Draining Decoction, Job's Tears Decoction, or Peony Decoction. If the lips and tongue are scorched and dry with sores in the mouth, this is caused by heat affecting the heart and spleen. Soak Huanglian in water and promptly drink it. If there is great thirst with little drinking, use Bamboo Leaf and Gypsum Decoction.

Three Causes Formulas
Chen Wuzhe, Song Dynasty

Loss of Cheek Muscle Control

For any issues with the cheeks unable to properly open and close due to a fall, have the individual drink alcohol until heavily intoxicated. While they sleep, blow powdered, dried fruit into their nostrils to induce sneezing, and they will return to normal.

Six Writings from Hejian
Liu Wanshu, Jin Dynasty

Bitter Mouth

When one is indecisive and the gallbladder is deficient, causing qi to rise, the sensation of bitterness in the mouth occurs. The mouth is the residence of clarity; when disturbed by turbid qi, it overflows, which the Gallbladder-Enriching Decoction can remedy.[15p]

Oral Ulcer

Heat from the bladder transfers to the small intestine, causing obstruction in the diaphragm and intestines, leading to oral ulcers. When heart and stomach are obstructed by heat, food and water do not digest and move downward into the small intestine. The remedy is Chaihu-Digupi Decoction.
Rumen's Filial Piety, by Zhang Congzheng (Yuan Dynasty)

Mouth Sores

For adults and children with mouth sores and tight lips, wash away the white scabs with sour plum water, and when in distress, apply Qingpao powder. If it does not heal, apply Yuyan powder. If still not healed, use Qianbai powder for recovery.
The Ten Books of Dongyuan, by Li Gao (Yuan Dynasty)

Differentiating Between Food, Drink, Labor, and Injury

If injury arises from food, drink, or labor, the symptoms will be evident in the mouth: loss of taste, abdominal discomfort, unwillingness to speak; even when forced to respond, the voice will be weak. There will be excessive saliva in the mouth and clear nasal discharge, which may be intermittent; this indicates a Yin condition. The mouth corresponds to the Earth element; the spleen's energy connects to it. If food intake is irregular, and injury arises from labor, the mouth cannot discern flavors, nor can it recognize the five tastes. It can also be said that harmful food is evidently the cause of the issue.

Oral Ulcer

The classic states: Heat from the bladder moves to the small intestine, causing discomfort in the diaphragm and intestines, leading to oral ulcers. This condition is common among people who drink alcohol frequently. It is advisable to use Wuling powder and Daohong powder together; it proves effective.
Danxi's Heart Methods, by Zhu Zhenheng (Yuan Dynasty)[16p]
Mouth Ulcers

For mouth ulcers that do not heal with cold medicine, it is due to the deficiency of the middle jiao and difficulty in eating, with the fire of the yang rising unrestrained. Use the Li Zhong Decoction. Ginseng, white atractylodes, and licorice can replenish the deficiency of the earth; dry ginger can disperse the fire. If severe, add aconite. It is also effective to suck on fragrant cassia; or grind alum into powder and apply it; or hold it in the mouth and rinse with water repeatedly; for severe cases, drink watermelon juice slowly. In winter, if watermelon is unavailable, use burnt watermelon rind ash; or boil huanglian with good wine and sip it for immediate relief. All mouth and tongue sores arise from heat accumulation in the upper jiao. It is advisable to use Sheng Tang; or sweet tangerine soup with a money of yellow qin, and still combine it with willow flower powder.

Variations in Mouth Tastes: Sour, Bitter, Odorous, Spicy, Salty

Heat in the liver causes a sour taste in the mouth, as wood overcomes the spleen, making the mouth also sour. For this, Xiao Chai Hu Decoction is appropriate, adding gentian root and green peel; if severe, consider Danggui Longhui Pills. Heat in the heart causes bitterness or ulcers in the mouth; for this, use Liangge San or Xiexin Decoction. If heat from the liver transfers to the gallbladder, the mouth will also taste bitter. Use Xiao Chai Hu Decoction, adding stem of wheat, sour jujube seed, root of dilong, and yuan zhi. If sputum is purulent and blood-streaked like a lung abscess, with foul breath, and other treatments are ineffective, use the Xiaofeng San; mix into gray millet with clear rice drink for relief, two doses can clear it.

If heat is in the lungs, the mouth will taste spicy; use sweet tangerine soup or Xie Bai San. If heat is in the kidneys, the mouth will taste salty; use Zhi Shen Wan or Zi Yin Da Bu Wan.

— Hygienic Treasure Mirror by Luo Tianyi in the Yuan Dynasty.[17p]

Discussion on Oral Lesions

According to the theory of reversed conditions: Heat from the bladder transfers to the small intestine, causing discomfort in the diaphragm and intestines, resulting in oral lesions. When the heart and stomach are blocked by heat, food and water do not circulate properly and are transmitted down to the small intestine. The Dan Zhi San disperses heat from the small intestine, while the Wu Ling San drains heat from the bladder; thus, the Dan Zhi San is used in conjunction with the Wu Ling San.
— Effective Formulas from Contemporary Physicians [Yuan Dynasty, Wei Yilin]

When Qi of the Viscera is Deficient, It Reflects in the Mouth

The taste perceived in the mouth is affected by dominant heat (which presents as bitterness) or dominant cold (which presents as saltiness). Accumulated food leads to sourness, irritability leads to dryness, deficiency presents as blandness, abscesses as sweetness, exhaustion causes bad breath, and stagnation results in sores. The saliva of the mouth connects to the five organs; when the Qi of the organs is dominant, the corresponding tastes manifest in the mouth.
— Remarkable Effective Formulas [Ming Dynasty, Fang Xian]

General Discussion

The mouth is the channel of the Taiyin meridian, governed by the spleen, and is where the five flavors enter. When flavors are ingested, they are stored in the stomach and spleen, transforming into fluids to nourish the five types of Qi, which correspond to the five organs. When the balance of the five Qi is disrupted, various illnesses arise. For instance, saltiness is associated with cold, sourness with stagnation, dryness with irritability, blandness with deficiency, and heat is related to both bitterness and sweetness. Bad breath indicates dryness and decay in the viscera. Heat accumulates between the chest and diaphragm, resulting in oral manifestations. Oral sores arise from stagnation of spleen Qi, exacerbated by wind and heat. Treatment methods should be adapted according to their causes.[18p]
Mouth Ulcers

Mouth ulcers arise from excess heat in the upper heater, deficient cold in the middle heater, and yin fire in the lower heater, caused by changes in the meridians, and should be treated accordingly. If there is fever and thirst, and the patient drinks cold, it indicates excess heat. For mild cases, use Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang; for severe cases, use Liu Jun Zi Tang. If there is little appetite with loose stools and a lack of central energy, it indicates deficiency of qi; use Ren Shen Li Zhong Tang. If the hands and feet feel cold while the abdomen is painful, it indicates deficiency of cold qi; use Fu Zi Li Zhong Tang. If there is evening heat and internal heat without a consistent pattern, it indicates blood deficiency; use Ba Zhen Tang with Dan Pi, Wu Wei, and Mai Men Dong. If there is thirst with sputum and frequent urination, it indicates deficiency of kidney water; use Jia Jian Ba Wei Wan. If there is little food intake and loose stools, with a pale face and cold limbs, it indicates deficiency of heat and earth; use Ba Wei Wan. If there is evening fever that starts in the abdomen, it indicates yin deficiency; use Si Wu Tang with Ren Shen, Bai Zhu, Wu Wei, and Mai Men Dong, and avoid Jia Jian Ba Wei Wan. If the heat comes and goes, visible during the day and hidden at night, with an inconsistent pattern, sometimes starting in the feet, it indicates a rootless fire; use the previous prescriptions, along with Shi Quan Da Bu Tang with Mai Men Dong and Wu Wei, and apply powdered Fu Zi mixed with saliva to the Yong Quan point. If one uses cold and cool treatments indiscriminately, it will damage vital energy, leading to significant harm.[19p]
Introduction to Medicine [Ming Dynasty, Li Zhan]

General Discussion on Oral Diseases

Heat in the spleen leads to a sweet or foul taste in the mouth, and treatment should be with Huang San or San Huang Decoction. If there is heat in the stomach, the mouth may taste sweet; if the stomach is weak, the taste may be bland. Heat in the liver results in a sour taste, and when wood invades the spleen, the mouth also tastes sour. For this, Xiao Chai Hu Decoction with Cao Long Dan and Qing Pi is advisable; in severe cases, Dang Gui Long Hui Pill should be used. Heat in the lungs causes a spicy taste, so Gan Ju Decoction or Xie Bai San is recommended. Heat in the kidneys results in a salty taste, for which Zhi Shen Wan or Zhi Yin Da Bu Wan is suitable. Bad breath indicates stomach heat, where deficiency fire accumulates within the chest, leading to halitosis; in this case, use Xiong Zhi Gao. If the stomach’s yang is injured, the mouth will be tasteless; if the kidney’s yin is deficient, a taste will remain in the mouth.

Key Points in Diagnosis and Treatment [Ming Dynasty, Dai Si Gong]

Oral Ulcers

Ulcers on the tongue and inside the mouth are caused by heat obstructing the upper jiao. The treatment should be Sheng Tang or Gan Ju Decoction with a penny of Huang Qin, along with apricot flower powder mixed in; if ineffective, add Si Xiang Drink. When there is deficiency below and excess above, causing oral ulcers, use stabilizing medications to reduce the yang light. It is advisable to use salt water for nourishing the Zheng Dan or He Yan Dan. Also, soak the feet in hot water before bed and pan-fry a small pinch of Wu Zhu Yu. After wiping the feet, apply the fried Zhi to the soles and bind with silk cloth, with men on the left and women on the right.[20p]
Examination of Medical Formulas 【Ming Dynasty, Wu Kun】

Discussion on Oral Diseases

For sores and ulcers in the mouth, "Kou Mi San" is the primary treatment. Mouth ulcers stem from damp-heat; if damp-heat does not dissipate, it will inevitably lead to decay. Cold can counteract heat, and bitter substances can strengthen the skin. Therefore, we use the powerful properties of Coptis chinensis, Huangbai, and realgar to kill pests and promote circulation; the cooling effects of ice brain deter pests and penetrate the pores; and the bitterness of myrrh disperses blood and heals wounds.

Master Sun, in the "Thousand Gold Formulas," says: "The root of wild rose is a divine medicine for mouth sores, which people do not know." Thus, for those with oral issues, using wild rose root is quite common. Now, I have tasted its medicinal aroma, which is harmonious yet bitter. The "Inner Canon" states: "Thin qi is the yin within yang," and further states, "A strong flavor causes leakage." This clearly indicates that it is a medicine to clear qi and dissipate heat.

According to the theory of qi convulsion: heat from the bladder is transferred to the small intestine, causing discomfort in the diaphragm and leading to mouth ulcers. The decoction of Bupleurum and Rehmannia is prescribed for this. The bladder is the outlet for water, while the small intestine is the region where clear and turbid substances are separated.[21p]
When the bladder transfers heat to the small intestine, the distinctions between clear and turbid cannot be made, and damp heat cannot be eliminated. This inevitably leads to an upward steaming, causing ulceration and sores in the mouth, resembling meat stew being boiled in a pot. In this formula, Chai Hu is pungent and warm, hence it elevates the clear yang; Di Gu Pi is bitter and cold, therefore it lowers the turbid yin. Once the clear and turbid are delineated, the dry clear and nourishing earth will restore the middle and allow bowel movements to be smooth, healing the mouth's sores.

For those with solid conditions, add Da Huang and (Shi Bu) Niao. This refers to constipation, where the pathogenic qi is solid. Both yin are obstructed, and the pathway is not open. Thus, Da Huang, being bitter and cold, is used to purge the solid condition, while (Shi Bu) Niao, being salty and cold, softens the hard masses, like drawing out the fire from the stove.

For indecision and weakness in the liver and gallbladder, leading to bitter taste and tongue sores, Yi Dan Tang is indicated. The liver governs deliberation, and the gallbladder governs decision-making. Being overburdened with thoughts leads to qi deficiency. The throat is linked to the gallbladder, and gallbladder bile overflowing into the throat results in a bitter mouth. The wood element can generate fire, leading to tongue sores.

In this formula, Ren Shen and Gan Cao are included to replenish the qi deficiency; Ku Shen and Huang Qin help clear the heat from the qi. The classic states: "When the ruler is clear, the lower will be peaceful." Therefore, Fu Shen and Yuan Zhi are used to nourish the heart. It also states: "In minor cases treat directly, in severe cases treat indirectly." Hence, Gui Zhi's pungent warmth is utilized.[22p]

The Principles of Diagnosis and Treatment 【Ming Dynasty, Wang Kentang】

Pertaining to the Lips

The lips belong to the foot Taiyin spleen meridian.
Note: "The Spleen is the root of the granaries, the residence of nourishment; its manifestation is in the lips." (from the "Suwen")
"The Spleen governs defense, guiding the reception of food, and observing the state of the lips and tongue to discern fortune." (from the "Lingshu")
Thus, when the lips are well-proportioned, the spleen is balanced; when the lips are unevenly positioned, the spleen is unsteady; if the lips are retracted, the spleen is elevated; if the lower lips are enlarged, the spleen is deficient; firm lips indicate a strong spleen, while large and soft lips suggest a fragile spleen. In cases of spleen disease, the lips turn yellow; in severe spleen dysfunction, the lips swell on all sides. Additionally, "The lips and tongue are the basis of muscle. When the foot Taiyin qi is depleted, the pulse does not nourish the muscles; when the pulse does not nourish, the muscles soften. If the muscles are soft, the tongue atrophies, and the area between the lips fills out; when this area fills, the lips retract, indicating that the flesh is failing. The first element is Wood prevailing over Earth."

They also belong to the foot Yangming stomach meridian.
Note: "Diseases arising from the foot Yangming manifest as swollen lips." (from the "Lingshu") The swelling referred to as "swelling" is blood-related. "Swelling" is an ancient term for lip ulcer. Moreover, it is noted that when Yangming qi is present, it may cause lip chewing. "In the case of heat in the stomach, the lips turn black." (from "Zhuzhong")

They further belong to the hand Shaoyin heart meridian.
Note: "When both the upper and lower lips are red, it indicates heat in the heart." (from "Yuan Zhu") If the upper lip is red and the lower lip is white, it suggests kidney deficiency with heart fire not descending.

They also belong to the hand Shaoyin lung meridian.[23p]
Note: Qian Zhongyang said: The lungs govern the color white; if the lips are white and moist, it is auspicious, but if they are as pale as withered bones, it indicates death. White lips should be treated by nourishing the spleen and lungs, as the spleen is the mother of the lungs. If both mother and child are deficient and cannot nourish each other, this condition is called "timidity," thus they should be supplemented. If the color is deep red, then it is necessary to disperse the lung's excessive heat.

The lips are governed by the Chong and Ren meridians.

Note: The "Lingshu" says that the Chong and Ren meridians both originate in the uterus, follow the back, and are the seas of the meridians. The superficial paths circulate around the abdomen, ascending to meet at the throat, branching off to connect with the lips and mouth. Therefore, when vital energy and blood are abundant, the skin and flesh are warm and firm; when blood alone is abundant, it lightly penetrates the skin and produces fine hair. Women experiencing blood loss have excess energy but insufficient blood, leading to the Chong and Ren meridians not nourishing the lips, hence they appear thin.

The upper lip is associated with the Hand Yangming Large Intestine Meridian.
The lower lip is associated with the Foot Yangming Stomach Meridian.

In summary:

The mouth is governed by the spleen and is interlinked with the stomach and large intestine meridians.

The classics say: The center is yellow; it connects to the spleen, opens at the mouth, and stores essence in the spleen. Further, it states that the spleen governs the mouth; as an organ, it is the spleen, and as an orifice, it is the mouth. Again, the classic states that the spleen's energy connects to the mouth; when the spleen is harmonious, the mouth can discern the five flavors. This is how the spleen governs the mouth. Additionally, the classics say that the Stomach's Foot Yangming Meridian connects below the mouth and meets at the Chengjiang point. And, the Large Intestine's Hand Yangming Meridian connects at the mouth, meeting at the Renzhong point. This illustrates how the Stomach and Large Intestine meridians intersect at the mouth.[24p]

Treatment Methods for Various Symptoms

When dry, it becomes parched; when hot, it cracks; when windy, it trembles; when cold, it peels. If the lips swell and turn white, and the skin is wrinkled and cracked like a silkworm cocoon, this is termed "cocoon lips." Some cases have lips swollen like a cocoon, while others have a fine root larger than a cocoon or a lump. This can be caused by emotional disturbances igniting fire and damaging blood, by heart fire affecting the spleen channel, or by excessive flavors accumulating heat and harming the spleen.

The essential point is to assess the primary condition and consider any accompanying issues. Nourishing spleen qi to generate spleen blood will lead to moisture returning and fire being extinguished, causing wind to dissipate and swelling to subside. If the patient neglects this or if the practitioner fails to recognize the situation, recklessly using clearing heat and detoxifying medications, or improperly applying treatment, could lead to exacerbation of symptoms.

For kidney deficiency causing lip cocoons, with occasional bleeding and internal heat leading to dry mouth, phlegm, and weight loss, "Jiyi Yin Dihuang Wan" should be used.

For liver channel heat due to anger, with wind heat affecting the spleen causing swelling and cracking of the lips, "Chai Hu Qing Gan San" should be indicated.

For stomach fire leading to blood dryness, resulting in cracking lips and painful gum ulcers, "Qing Wei San" is appropriate, possibly adding Paeonia and Angelica or Chai Hu to address heat in the spleen, stomach, liver, and gallbladder channels.

If wind heat spreads to the spleen, causing trembling and wrinkling of the lips, along with dizziness or swelling of the limbs resembling wind, "Qiang Huo San" is recommended.

For wind heat stagnating in the spleen channel leading to dry and cracked lips without color, "Xie Huang Yin Zi" should be used.

In cases of damaged central qi causing sores on the lips and mouth, chills and fever, along with a feeling of fatigue, "Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang" is advised.

If worry and overthinking harm the spleen, depleting blood and causing wrinkled lips, "Gui Pi Tang" is appropriate.[25p]
Excessive thinking generates heat in the spleen, leading to symptoms like dry lips and mouth, ulceration, and long-lasting sores. For internal treatment, take the Five Blessings Detoxification Pill; for external treatment, use ashes from roasted olives mixed with pig fat for application, or finely grind the kernel and apply it.

For sweet taste in the mouth, use raw Rehmannia, Peony, Coptis, and Sanhuang Pill. For bitter taste in the mouth, use Bupleurum, Scutellaria, Coptis, Sophora, Gentian, and Xiao Chai Hu Decoction, adding Ophiopogon, sour jujube seed, Rehmannia root, and Polygala. The Inner Canon states that a bitter mouth signifies gallbladder obstruction. The liver governs planning, and the gallbladder governs decision-making; an excess of bile leads to the gallbladder becoming indecisive, causing anger, which results in qi rebounding and bile overflowing, hence the bitter taste. If the heat is severe, use Long Dan Decoction to address it.[26p]
Mouth Ulcers

Mouth ulcers, also known as heat. The classics state: when the lesser yang governs the heavens, fire energy descends, and lung energy ascends, this leads to mouth ulcers. The second type is cold. The classics say: when the yearly metal does not suffice, the fiery heat progresses, subsequently cold rain violently arrives, the yin is blocked, and the yang rises, resulting in the disease of mouth ulcers.

Someone may ask how mouth ulcers are caused. It is said: the classics explain that the bladder transfers heat to the small intestine, causing the diaphragm and intestines to be obstructed, leading to oral sores. The small intestine is the organ related to the heart; this situation arises due to the influence of evil heat. The heart is associated with the sovereign fire, the main organ among the five viscera and six bowels. Thus, all the heat from the classics corresponds to the heart; the heart's channels are distributed to the tongue. If heart fire rises excessively and vaporizes in the mouth, it causes sores on the tongue. The spleen's channels are distributed beneath the tongue; if spleen heat generates phlegm, and heated saliva interacts, rising from the fire, ulcers can also occur, often in greater numbers.

For both conditions, all cold and cool agents can treat them, but if there is saliva, it is necessary to also address the saliva. What then if someone uses a middle-of-the-road decoction with added aconite to treat it? It is said: fire has both deficiency and excess. When there is originally heat in the channels, but it moves excessively, this is called excess; when it moves without heat, this is called deficiency. For excess, the correct treatment is with cold and cool agents; for deficiency, the treatment should be with warmth. The middle-of-the-road decoction is used when the stomach is deficient and the grain is sparse, thereby opposing the counteracting kidney water energy, turning into cold internally.[27p]
When the spleen and stomach are weak and their fire is forced to rise, resulting in mouth sores, ginseng, Atractylodes, and licorice are used to nourish the earth, while ginger and Aconite are used to dispel the cold, allowing the fire to receive assistance and retreat. In the "Sheng Ji Zong Lu," it is said that for a cold deficiency of the original organs that leads to mouth sores, one should use a powder of Ba Jiu, Bai Zhi, and Gao Liang Jiang, along with cooked pig kidney. There are also methods using clove, pepper, pine resin, powdered Xixin, and Su Mu decoction to apply to the sores. For those who cannot eat, angelica, Aconite, and white honey should be sucked and swallowed; some apply fresh Aconite to the soles of the feet, or use powdered Wu Zhu Yu boiled with vinegar to create a paste, mixed with fresh Dihong to apply to the soles of both feet. These methods are all for treating the fire of the dragon. It is due to cold water pressing up that the yang of the heart and lungs cannot descend, hence warm and hot remedies are utilized, either dispersing upward or downward, or benefiting from the yin following the yang.

If there is heat in the stomach and the pulse is strong and large, it is advisable to take Liang Ge San, Gan Ju Tang with three Supplement Pills of Huang Qin, Jin Hua Wan, rinse with Huang Lian Sheng Ma Tang, and apply Lv Pao San or Mi Bo San. Dan Xi recommends slowly drinking watermelon juice; if there is nothing to burn the skin to powder, apply powdered Xixin and Huang Lian mixed into it externally.

According to the Hu family's prescription, finely grind a weevil and apply it, which is effective immediately. This is deemed the correct remedy for transferring heat from the bladder to the small intestine. The weevil specifically travels to the small intestine and bladder, opening the pathways; it has a potent and strong energy, which may lead to sores from yin deficiency and upward-ascending energy, thus should be avoided unless there is substantial heat in the upper jiao.[28p]
Surgical Classic 【Ming Dynasty – Chen Shigong】

Lip Wind

When the stomach fire of the Yangming channel ascends, it causes itching and swelling of the lower lip, leading to cracking and weeping without pain, making it difficult to heal. One should use a copper powder pill for soaking and washing, and internally take the Liuwei Dihuang Wan for self-healing.

Chapped Lips

Chapped lips are a manifestation of the Yangming stomach channel. They occur due to overeating fried and scorched foods, coupled with intense worry and anxiety, which causes phlegm to follow the fire, accumulating in the lips. Initially, it resembles a bean and gradually enlarges like a silkworm cocoon, becoming swollen and hard. In severe cases, it becomes painful, hinders eating, may rupture and bleed, and over time can lead to diabetes or difficult-to-treat internal conditions.

For early stages or established cases without internal issues, use large moxa sticks on the affected area, apply a toad venom cake, and cover with a plaster; over time, this will gradually dissipate. For those with thirst as an internal issue, it is advisable to take Jiawei Bamei Wan early and drink Qingliang Ganlu beverage at noon to nourish the source of digestion. If bleeding persists for an extended period, leading to weakness, internal heat with phlegm, a dark complexion, red cheeks, and severe dryness and thirst, it indicates a condition that is difficult to treat.[29p]
Mouth Ulcers

Mouth ulcers can be categorized into deficient fire and excess fire, as well as pale color and red color. Deficient fire appears pale with white spots and fine dots; in severe cases, it shows crack-like patterns resembling turtle shells, with a weak pulse and no thirst. This is caused by excessive worry, with more wakefulness than sleep, leading to the eruption of deficient fire. It is treated with Si Wu Decoction combined with Lian Qiao, Zhimu, Dan Pi, and Rougui to guide the treatment. Externally, it is treated by applying willow flower powder. Excess fire, on the other hand, appears red with deep ulcers in the mouth, and in severe cases, the cheeks and tongue swell, the pulse is full, and there is dry mouth. This is caused by rich foods, thick flavors, and strong alcoholic beverages that provoke the heart fire. It is advisable to use Liangge Powder, and externally apply Fuyan Powder; expelling saliva will lead to improvement. If there are ulcers on the tongue, and it is dry, yellow, and hard with thirst, the Bawei Pill should be adjusted to nourish the source of digestion, and water rinsing should be avoided.

Method for Treating Drooping Chin

Drooping chin occurs due to Qi deficiency, which prevents the closure of the orifice. Instruct the patient to sit upright, supporting the chin with both hands, placing the thumbs inside the mouth, pressing on the upper molars tightly against the lower cheeks, and using force to press downward towards the shoulders, sending energy upwards to the back of the head. Then, use a silk strip to wrap around the chin at the top for about half an hour, and then remove it; this will result in recovery.[30p]
The Complete Book of Jingyue (Ming, Zhang Jiebin)

The Disease of Thirst and Dryness

There is a significant difference between thirst and dryness, but many people cannot discern this. Thirst arises from an excess of fire and dryness from insufficient fluids. An excess of fire should be treated as real heat; insufficient fluids should be treated as a deficiency of yin. If these two conditions are not distinguished, it is akin to mixing ice and fire. However, although thirst is related to fire, there are several types that should be recognized: for instance, thirst from real heat, which indicates excess fire; and thirst from lacking yin, which indicates insufficient water. Therefore, following a significant loss of fluids due to severe diarrhea, heavy sweating, great exertion, major illness, postpartum blood loss, major boils, and after overeating salty foods, all can lead to thirst. All these cases stem from loss of yin and fluids, resulting in diminished water and dryness, and are not a manifestation of heat, so they should not be misinterpreted as fire symptoms. In summary, if one feels thirsty and likes cold drinks, with a strong pulse that feels bound, this is indeed a sign of fire. If cold drinks lead to stagnation and they prefer hot drinks while having a weak pulse and loose stool, this is not a fire symptom. Furthermore, those with dry mouths may experience bitterness but have no desire for tea or soup; this indicates dryness, not thirst. This particularly pertains to signs of yin deficiency; if one treats this condition as thirst, how can it be without error? Therefore, the method of treatment should focus on clearing heat from the lungs and stomach if fire is prevalent above; and if water is deficient below, one should replenish the spleen and kidneys. If yang is deficient and there is no means for yin to generate, and if qi is deficient and essence cannot transform, then without a harmonious balance of water and fire, what benefit could there be?[31p]
The Taste of Bitterness and Sourness

The symptoms of a bitter or sour mouth are all attributed to heat in the "Yuan Bing Shi." It states that liver heat leads to a sour mouth, heart heat to a bitter mouth, spleen heat to a sweet mouth, lung heat to a spicy mouth, and kidney heat to a salty mouth. If the mouth is bland, it is also due to stomach heat. According to this reasoning, all instances of the five tastes in the mouth would belong to heat syndromes, with no possibility of deficiency or cold diseases—could this not be erroneous? For instance, a bitter mouth does not necessarily come solely from heart fire; a bland mouth is not solely caused by stomach heat. In fact, excessive thinking and fatigue, as well as excessive desires, often lead to symptoms of a bitter mouth and dry tongue, with a lack of taste in food. Such issues do not stem from the heart or spleen, but rather from the liver and kidneys. If the heart and spleen are deficient, the liver and gallbladder can overflow with evil and cause bitterness; if the liver and kidneys are deficient, a lack of true yin results in dryness. Similarly, a bland mouth can arise after great labor, severe diarrhea, excessive sweating, or serious illness, which certainly does not mean it is solely due to stomach fire, does it? Therefore, when encountering such cases, one should examine whether there are no other heat syndromes or heat pulses, and it would be inappropriate to hastily assume internal heat caused by overexertion and recklessly use cold treatments.[32p]
Foul Breath

Although bad breath is caused by stomach heat, there are also non-heat variations. The foul smell from stomach heat is indeed filthy and often accompanies symptoms like dry mouth and heat in the mouth, as well as other signs of Yangming fire. However, if there are no signs of fire and the smell resembles that of rotten food or sourness, with symptoms like sourness in the stomach and tongue, or food stagnation with belching, it indicates the stench of dampness retaining filth, which is different from the heat-related foulness. This suggests issues related to failure of thoughts and a weakened spleen unable to transform food. Thus, we have one case of Yang syndrome that should clear stomach heat, and another of Yin syndrome that should nourish the heart and spleen. It is incorrect to assume that all foulness must be heat-related, as this could lead to other illnesses.

Presence or Absence of Heat

Diseases of the mouth and tongue can manifest as sores, foulness, dryness, thirst, or a variety of bitter and sour tastes. While many classical texts categorize oral diseases as heat-related, there are also conditions resembling heat but not truly heat-related, as well as fatigue without fire, which cannot all be classified as heat-related.[33p]
Mouth Ulcers

Mouth and tongue sores are mostly caused by heat in the upper burner, and treatment should focus on clearing heat. However, if there is excessive fatigue due to alcohol consumption, accompanied by a weak pulse and insufficient central qi, then cold and cooling methods will not be effective. Therefore, after prolonged use of cooling methods without results, one should investigate the underlying causes. An approach may involve tonifying the heart and spleen, nourishing kidney water, using Li Zhong Decoction, or employing honey and prepared Aconite; only then can one achieve complete recovery. This illustrates the need to distinguish between cold and heat.

Treatment Method

For mouth ulcers with a bitter taste, and for symptoms of heat in the three burners, sweet dew drink or Xi Xin drink should be used. In cases of severe heat, Cool the Diaphragm Powder or Yuan Shen Powder should be employed. If there is excess stomach fire, use Bamboo Leaf and Gypsum Decoction or San Huang Pill. For heart and liver fire, use Xie Xin Decoction or Long Dan Xie Gan Decoction. In cases of damp heat from alcohol leading to oral ulcers, Da Duan Qing Drink, Da Fen Qing Drink, or Wu Ling Powder should be prescribed. If there’s damage to the heart and spleen with accompanying fire, Er Yin Decoction or Qing Xin Lotus Seed Drink may be used. If one’s thoughts and plans are frustrated leading to liver and gallbladder deficiency with bitterness in the mouth, Qi Fu Drink, Li Yin Decoction, or Wu Jun Zi Decoction may be administered. If there is excessive fire, herbs like Huang Qin and Long Dan Cao should be added as needed.[34p]
For cases of mouth sores with six pulses weak, or those that don't improve after long use of cold remedies, it is essential to address the underlying rootless heat. One should consider treatments like Yin decoctions or the Principle Middle Soup. Using cassia to chew and swallow is also acceptable.

For external treatment of mouth sores, options include Yin-Yang Powder, Green Cloud Powder, Xixin and Huangbo Powder, and White Silkworm and Huangbo Powder. It can also be effective to hold Sichuan Huangbo in the mouth overnight. If there are sores and ulcers on the tongue, Ice Jade Powder should be administered. For decay due to improper diet, Ice White Powder is recommended. If bad breath is due to stomach heat, treatments like Stomach Clearing Decoction, Shengma and Huanglian Pill, or Bamboo Leaf and Gypsum Decoction with fragrance should be used; or the Thousand Gold Bad Breath Formula can help clear the heat internally. Furthermore, options like Clove Pill, Holy Benefit Tooth Formula, and Fujian Fragrant Tea Cakes can temporarily alleviate the foulness.[35p]
Secret Formula of the Stone Chamber
[Qing Dynasty - Chen Shiduo]

Mouth Sores

Mouth and tongue sores arise from the accumulation of heart fire. Take three qian of Huanglian and one qian of Changpu, decoct in water and take as a single dose to achieve cure; this is a marvelous formula. The uniqueness of this remedy lies not in Huanglian but in Changpu. Changpu is a medicine that leads to the heart channel. Although Huanglian also enters the heart channel, it inevitably involves the liver and spleen, whereas Changpu solely targets the heart. Furthermore, without being mixed with medicines from other channels, it acts decisively; thus, there is no doubt of its efficacy. This is why it works so effectively. If one does not understand the subtleties of using these herbs and mixes them with liver and spleen medicines, although they may still work, they will ultimately not be as swift as a beating drum. This is yet another method for treating heat. When sores appear on the mouth or tongue, light and clear substances should be used, applying them sparingly will yield immediate effects, similar to the formula of Xiao Chai Hu Decoction. However, many do not understand the balance in this formula; I will refine it further, so it may serve as a lasting model.[36p]
Take one dram of Chai Hu, one dram of Huang Qin, one dram of Ban Xia, five cents of Chen Pi, and one dram of Gan Cao. This is Xiao Chai Hu Decoction. I further add five cents of Ren Shen and two drams of Fu Ling to make it even more extraordinary. When qi is sufficient, evil can easily be expelled, and sweating can easily occur. People in the world see the use of Ren Shen and feel faint, not only do physicians hesitate to use it, but even patients are afraid to take it, leading to a situation where many remain incurable. How can we spread the word to all the doctors in the world to carefully investigate the source of illness and use it wisely?

For those with sores in the mouth, it is due to heat in the heart channel. It is advisable to use cooling herbs like Huang Lian and Huang Qin to disperse the heat, and they will heal naturally. However, currently, there is none used. Use one dram of Huang Bo, one dram of Jiang Can, five cents of scorched Zhi Ke, five cents of honey-fried Gan Cao powder, five cents of mint powder, three grains of Bing Pian, and five cents of Shan Dou Gen, all powdered finely. Soak this mixture, apply three times a day. By the first day, there will be quick relief; by the next day, full recovery. This is a miraculous formula. The above is a method for treating serious conditions.[37p]
Cleft Lip

When a person experiences extreme heat, their tongue feels like a thorn, and their lips and mouth crack, leading to intense thirst and a call for drink. Although this condition is not caused by a fever, anyone suffering from this illness, even without a fever, will not survive for long. Bai Hu Tang can also provide relief; however, if it is too cold, it may harm the stomach's energy, often resulting in a reduction of heat that leads to further complications, ultimately resulting in demise. Therefore, Bai Hu Tang should not be used lightly.

I have a remedy called Qing Liang San: two taels of Yuanshen, one tael of Maidong, five qian each of Chamomile and Qinghao, three qian each of White Mustard Seed, Shengdi, and Cheqianzi, all boiled in water for consumption. The brilliance of this formula lies in the fact that Yuanshen serves as the monarch to relieve the fires of the upper jiao; Maidong acts as the minister to resolve the heat in the lungs. Chamomile and Qinghao serve as assistants to eliminate the fire in the stomach. Particularly remarkable are Cheqianzi, White Mustard Seed, and Shengdi as emissaries, either transforming phlegm or cooling the blood, all of which help expel the great heat from below the bladder. This way, the balance between the upper and lower parts of the body remains cool, dispelling heat without harming the stomach. Thus, it can support the critically ill without causing complications.[38p]
Mouth Ulcer Formulas

General

For treating mouth ulcers: Take one liang of fivefold galla, honey-fried huangbo, and five qian each of purple talc; grind them together as powder. Take half a qian each time and mix it in the mouth for remarkable results.

Red and White Mouth Ulcer Formula

Mix equal parts of huangbo, qingdai, and mitoseng, and grind them into powder to apply.

Painful Mouth Ulcer Formula

Equal parts of huanglian, huangbo, huangqin, zhiszi, xixin, and dried ginger, ground into powder; first rinse the mouth with rice wash, and then apply the powder. Another formula for treating earlier symptoms consists of equal parts of xixin and fried huangbo, ground into powder and applied into the mouth, leading to immediate relief.

Jianjin Powder

For treating heat toxins that produce mouth and tongue ulcers: equal parts of huanglian and xixin, ground into powder; first, wrap a cloth, dip it in water, and clean the affected area, then apply the medicine. Spitting saliva will result in healing.[39p]
Huangbai San (from "Hui Chun")
Treats mouth sores and oral ulcers effectively.
Equal parts of Huangbai, Haire Tea, and dried white alum, ground into powder. First, rinse the mouth with cold rice broth, then apply the powder.

Lvpao San (from "Yi Jian")
Treats mouth sores.
One ounce of honey-roasted Huangbai, three qian of Qingshu, and two fen of Pian Nao, ground into powder. Apply to the affected area; if saliva is expelled, it will heal.

Bixue (from "De Xiao", same below)
Treats sores on the tongue and mouth, tongue stiffness, swollen cheeks, and throat blockage.
Equal parts of Puhuang, Qingshu, Borsal, Yanshao, and Licorice, ground into powder. With a finger, apply to the mouth and swallow saliva.

Huanjin San
Treats toxic heat mouth sores.
Equal parts of Dried Ginger and Huanglian, ground into powder. Apply to the sore; initially, it may be intolerable, but it will soon heal.

Ruxiang San (from "Gang Mu", same below)
Treats red mouth sores.
One qian each of Ruxiang and Myrrh, half a qian of white alum, and a little copper green, ground into powder and applied.

Myrrh San
Treats white mouth sores.
One qian each of Myrrh, Ruxiang, and Xionghuang, half a qian of Qingfen, and a little Boduoshuang, ground into powder and applied.

Qingjin San (Danxi)
Treats acute and severe white mouth sores, resembling wood ear mushrooms.
Four qian each of Wubeizi and Qingshu, ground into powder. Mix with oil and apply to the sore; for ulcers in the throat, blow in using a bamboo tube, expelling saliva.[40p]
Zhu Yu San
Treats mouth sores and throat pain.
Grind equal parts of wuzhuyu (dried fruit) and dilong (earthworm) into a powder. Mix with rice vinegar and living yeast, apply to the soles of the feet for effective results. Alternatively, use just wuzhuyu powder mixed with water and apply to the soles of the feet for recovery as well.

Ru Sheng San
Treats mouth sores in children who cannot suckle.
Take one or two seeds of pian (a type of bean), remove the skin and crush it without removing the oil. Add a little cinnabar and realgar, apply to a piece of paper, part the hair on the child's forehead, and place it on the fontanelle. If blisters form around the edges, use warm water to wash off the medicine, then wash with calamus water to ensure safety, as if by divine intervention.

Po Xue Dan
Heavenly flower powder three taels, red peony two taels, ginger, and white atractylodes each one tael. Grind together into a powder, and use a small amount to dry sprinkle or mix with honey for application.

Long Dan Xie Gan Tang
Treats bitter mouth.
Use one qian each of chihou, fresh licorice, ginseng, tianmendong (asparagus), maidong (ophiopogon), huanglian (coptis), huangqin (scutellaria), grass gentian, and shanzhizhi (gardenia seed), five fen each; seven grains of wuweizi (schisandra). Grind together into one dose and decoct in water to take on an empty stomach. Avoid spicy and hot foods.

Yi Dan Tang He Jian
Treats indecision, liver Qi deficiency, and bitter mouth.
Use one qian each of huangqin (scutellaria), ginseng, and licorice; seven fen each of yuanzi (polygala) without bones, guanggui (cinnamon), three fen each of ku shen (bitter herb) and fu shen (poria). Grind together into one dose and decoct in water for consumption.[41p]
San Huang Decoction (from Hui Chun)
Treats heat in the spleen and sweet taste in the mouth.
Ingredients: Huang Lian, Huang Qin, Zhi Zi, Shi Gao, Bai Shao Yao, Ju Gen, Chen Pi, and Fu Ling, each 8 fen; Bai Zhu and Gan Cao, each 3 fen. Grind together to make one dose, add one Wu Mei, and decoct in water for consumption.

Xiong Zhi Ointment (from De Xiao)
Treats bad breath due to heat.
Ingredients: Chuan Xiong and Bai Zhi, ground to equal parts, mix with honey to form pills the size of Qian Shi. Each pill should be melted in the mouth before bedtime.

Jia Jian Gan Lu Decoction (from Ben Shi)
Treats stomach heat, bad breath, oral sores, and gum swelling.
Ingredients: Shu Di Huang, Sheng Di Huang, Tian Men Dong, Huang Qin, Pi Pa Ye, Yin Chen, Zhi Ke, Shi Hu, and Gan Cao, each 1 liang; Xi Jiao 3 qian. Grind to powder, and decoct 2 qian in water for consumption. This formula contains Xi Jiao which is particularly effective.

Sheng Ma Huang Lian Pill (from Zheng Chuan)
Treats foul breath that repels others.
Ingredients: Huang Qin washed in wine, 2 liang; Huang Lian 1 liang; ginger juice, lotus flower, Qing Pi, and Sheng Ma, each 5 qian; Sheng Gan Cao 2 qian; Bai Dan Xiang 1 qian. Grind together to make into pills the size of a marble, chew well and take with warm water.

Chai Hu Di Gu Pi Decoction He Jian
Treats bladder transfer heat to the small intestine, causing oral ulcers.
Ingredients: Chai Hu and Di Gu Pi, each 2.5 qian. Grind and decoct in water for consumption.[42p]
Liang Ge San (Return to Spring)
For treating excess heat in the Sanjiao, leading to sores in the mouth and tongue.
Ingredients: 1.2 grams of Forsythia, 7 grams each of Scutellaria, Cape Jasmine seed, Platycodon, Coptis, fresh Rehmannia, mint, Angelica, bitter orange peel, licorice, and red peony. Grind them together to make a paste, then decoct in water and take.

Yuzhi Yin Zi (Eastern Pavilion)
For treating heat in the diaphragm, sores in the mouth and tongue, and swollen throat.
Ingredients: 200 grams of processed licorice, 100 grams each of agastache leaves, gypsum, and Cape Jasmine seed. Grind everything into a fine powder, and take 3 grams mixed with fresh water.

Shengma Jian (Direct Instruction)
For treating heat in the heart and spleen, leading to cracked sores in the mouth and tongue.
Ingredients: 3 grams each of Cimicifuga, Scrophularia, Chuanxiong, fresh Rehmannia, and Ophiopogon, and 2.5 grams each of Coptis, rhubarb, Scutellaria, and licorice. Grind them to a paste, add 3 slices of ginger and 2 jujubes, and decoct in water.

Boron Granules
For treating mouth and tongue sores and bad breath.
Ingredients: 250 grams of cold water stone, 50 grams of boron powder, 10 grams of sodium bicarbonate, 5 grams each of borneol and musk. Grind to a fine powder, mix with 50 grams of licorice juice and cook into a paste, then form into pills the size of lotus seeds. Dissolve in the mouth or sprinkle the powder on.

Heishen Pills (Danxi)
For treating mouth and tongue sores that do not heal for years.
Ingredients: Equal parts of Scrophularia, Asparagus, and Ophiopogon, ground into powder, then made into honey pills the size of a marble. Dissolve one pill in the mouth each time.[43p]

Wu Ling San (by Zhang Zhongjing)
Treats oral ulcers.[44p]
Pigweed, Poria, and Atractylodes, each eighteen grains; Cinnamon six taels; Alisma one tael and six and a half grains. Grind these into a powder; take three qian each time.

Daohong Powder for the previous condition.
Raw Rehmannia, Akebia, and Licorice tips, equal parts, decoct in water to take.

Hu Huanglian Powder for the previous condition.
Hu Huanglian five fen, Agastache one qian, Asarum, Huanglian each three qian; grind these into a powder; take half a qian, dry sprinkle in the mouth, gargle and spit it out.

Biyue Powder for the previous condition.
Alumen and Rhubarb in equal parts; grind into a fine powder, apply dried in bed, let the saliva drain out, and gargle with warm water.

Huanglian Powder for the previous condition.
White silkworms, heated on a new tile to dry out the threads, remove the fire toxins; apply Huanglian honey, roast dry, remove the fire toxins; grind this extremely finely, a little sprinkled on the sore and on the tongue, to expel saliva.

Liangge Powder for mouth sores.
Forsythia four taels; Rhubarb soaked in wine; Glauber salt and Licorice each two taels; Gardenia roasted black, Huangqin roasted in wine, Mint each one tael; grind these into a powder; take three qian, add bamboo leaves and raw honey cooked together.

Ganjitang for the previous condition.
Platycodon one tael, Licorice two taels; decoct in water to take.

Sanbu Wan for the previous condition.
Huangqin, Huanglian, and Huangbai, ground into equal parts; make water pills, take thirty pills at a time, swallow with plain water.[45p]
Golden Flower Pill: For treating early symptoms.
Equal parts of Huanglian (Coptis), Huangbo (Phellodendron), Huangqin (Scutellaria), Zhizi (Gardenia), and Dahuang (Rhubarb) for constipation. Grind into powder, form into water pills, take thirty pills with warm water.

Huanglian Shengma Decoction: For treating early symptoms.
1.5 qian of Shengma (Cimicifuga), 3 qian of Huanglian (Coptis). Decoct with water, or grind into fine powder, wrap in cotton, and dissolve in saliva before swallowing.

Green Robe Powder: For treating early symptoms.
Four liang of Huangbo (Phellodendron) and two liang of roasted licorice, one liang of Qingsuan (indigo). First grind the two ingredients together, then mix with Qingsuan and dry for application.

Honey-leavened Powder:
No specific quantity for Huangbo; mix with honey to make a gray powder, and dry to use before sleeping. Avoid wine, vinegar, and sauce; if consumed, sores will be difficult to heal.

Huanglian Powder: For treating early symptoms.
5 qian each of Huanglian (Coptis), (Shibu) nitrate, and white alum; 1 liang of mint. Grind into coarse powder. Use the bile of a yellow cow from the twelfth month to contain the medicine, hang in the wind for two months. If there are mouth sores, grind the medicine finely and apply to the sores; it will cool the heat and saliva, leading to healing.

Toad Venom Cotton: For treating early symptoms.
Five pieces of toad venom (about the size of a soapberry), one piece each of borax, dragon brain (camphor), and musk (perfume of musk deer). Grind these into a fine powder, dissolve in half a cup of warm water, and mix with half a qian of red cotton. Dip the cotton in the medicinal juice and let it dry. When the medicinal juice is exhausted, cut the cotton into sections. Apply one piece to the affected area; if saliva is produced, expectorate. Repeat three to five times a day, replacing as needed, to achieve healing.[46p]
Huanglian Jiedu Decoction - for treating front symptoms.

  • Huanglian, Huangqin, Huangbo, and Guizhi in equal parts, decoct with water for consumption.

Yangzheng Dan - for treating front symptoms.

  • Grind one tael each of fine cinnabar, sulfur, mercury, and black lead. Use an iron bowl, burn charcoal to melt the lead into juice, add mercury, stir with willow sticks until mixed, then add the powdered cinnabar, stir until it is invisible. Lift it slightly, then add the sulfur powder, stir rapidly until it rises in flames. Sprinkle with vinegar, wait for it to cool, take out and grind into a very fine powder. Boil it with glutinous rice to make pills the size of mung beans. Each dose is seven fen, to be taken with salted water or red date soup; for individuals with deficient middle energy, use ginseng broth for ingestion.

Heixi Dan - for treating front symptoms.

  • Two taels each of black lead and sulfur, melt the lead gradually adding sulfur until it forms sheets; pour onto the ground to release fire toxins, and grind until silent.

Shengma Decoction - for treating mouth ulcers and rotten gums.

  • Half tael each of Shengma, Yuanshen, Huanglian, Huangqin, Gegen, Lingyangjiao powder, Dahuang, Qianghuo, Fangfeng, and chrysanthemum (remove core); two and a half qian each of ginseng, Zhimu, and roasted licorice. Grind together; each dose is three qian, boil in one cup of water until reduced to seven parts, strain, and take warm after meals. If ginseng is unavailable, substitute with burdock seeds.

Bingye Wan - for treating front symptoms.[47p]
A small amount of dragon brain, yellow foetid vine dried, borax ground, and peppermint leaves in equal parts. Grind into a fine powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of longan. Take one pill each time to promote saliva. For severe sores, add ground dragon brain.

Adjust and decrease the Xie Bai San for treating bad breath.

Three qian of mulberry root, two qian of platycodon, twenty-one grains of Schisandra, one and a half qian of wild yam and honey-prepared licorice, seven fen of anemarrhena, five fen each of scutellaria and ophiopogon. Chop these ingredients, boil with two cups of water until reduced to one cup, strain, and take warm, avoiding food for a while. Take twice daily. Avoid alcohol, damp, and spicy hot foods.

Shengxiang Ointment for treating hot and foul breath.

Dried sweet melon seeds, shelled and ground finely, mixed with a little honey to form a paste. After meals, hold in the mouth, or apply to the teeth for better effect. Another method: after rinsing the mouth, dissolve a pill the size of a jujube pit.

Dibugpi Pills for treating lung heat and bad breath, with a gummy mouth, dry tongue, thirst, and frequent urination.

Dibugpi, mulberry root, gardenia fruit, astragalus, and aristolochia in equal parts ground to a fine powder. Mix with licorice paste to form pills the size of fox nuts. Take one pill after meals to dissolve in the mouth.

Jipeili Huangyuan [Zhongjing] for treating intestinal water qi and dryness of the mouth and tongue.

Fangji, pepper eyes, flax, and rhubarb each one liang. Grind these four ingredients into a powder, form honey pills the size of a tung seed, and take one pill before meals, three times a day. If it slightly increases saliva, those feeling thirsty can add half a liang of mirabilite.[48p]
Danggui Longhui Pill: Treats liver heat and sour mouth.
Ingredients: Angelica (Danggui) washed in wine, Gentian root washed in wine, fried Gardenia fruit, fried Coptis, fried Gentianna, fried Baical skullcap, each one tael; big rhubarb soaked in wine, indigo flying powder, and aloe, each five qian; two qian of wood fragrance; five fen of musk. Prepare as a powder, make into pills with honey, take with ginger soup.

San Huang Pill: Treats sweet mouth.
Ingredients: Coptis, Baical skullcap, and big rhubarb, each nine times steamed and sun-dried, combined in equal portions, made into pills the size of a tung seed.

Xiao Chai Hu Decoction: Treats bitter mouth.
