Zhu Yu San
Treats mouth sores and throat pain.
Grind equal parts of wuzhuyu (dried fruit) and dilong (earthworm) into a powder. Mix with rice vinegar and living yeast, apply to the soles of the feet for effective results. Alternatively, use just wuzhuyu powder mixed with water and apply to the soles of the feet for recovery as well.

Ru Sheng San
Treats mouth sores in children who cannot suckle.
Take one or two seeds of pian (a type of bean), remove the skin and crush it without removing the oil. Add a little cinnabar and realgar, apply to a piece of paper, part the hair on the child's forehead, and place it on the fontanelle. If blisters form around the edges, use warm water to wash off the medicine, then wash with calamus water to ensure safety, as if by divine intervention.

Po Xue Dan

Grind together into one dose and decoct in water to take on an empty stomach. Avoid spicy and hot foods.

White silkworms, heated on a new tile to dry out the threads, remove the fire toxins; apply Huanglian honey, roast dry, remove the fire toxins; grind this extremely finely, a little sprinkled on the sore and on the tongue, to expel saliva.

Liangge Powder for mouth sores.
Forsythia four taels; Rhubarb soaked in wine; Glauber salt and Licorice each two taels; Gardenia roasted black, Huangqin roasted in wine, Mint each one tael; grind these into a powder; take three qian, add bamboo leaves and raw honey cooked together.

Ganjitang for the previous condition.
Platycodon one tael, Licorice two taels; decoct in water to take.

Sanbu Wan for the previous condition.
Huangqin, Huanglian, and Huangbai, ground into equal parts; make water pills, take thirty pills at a time, swallow with plain water.[45p]

Golden Flower Pill: For treating early symptoms.
Equal parts of Huanglian (Coptis), Huangbo (Phellodendron), Huangqin (Scutellaria), Zhizi (Gardenia), and Dahuang (Rhubarb) for constipation. Grind into powder, form into water pills, take thirty pills with warm water.

Huanglian Shengma Decoction: For treating early symptoms.
1.5 qian of Shengma (Cimicifuga), 3 qian of Huanglian (Coptis). Decoct with water, or grind into fine powder, wrap in cotton, and dissolve in saliva before swallowing.

Green Robe Powder: For treating early symptoms.
Four liang of Huangbo (Phellodendron) and two liang of roasted licorice, one liang of Qingsuan (indigo). First grind the two ingredients together, then mix with Qingsuan and dry for application.

Honey-leavened Powder:
No specific quantity for Huangbo; mix with honey to make a gray powder, and dry to use before sleeping. Avoid wine, vinegar, and sauce; if consumed, sores will be difficult to heal.

Huanglian Powder: For treating early symptoms.
5 qian each of Huanglian (Coptis), (Shibu) nitrate, and white alum; 1 liang of mint. Grind into coarse powder. Use the bile of a yellow cow from the twelfth month to contain the medicine, hang in the wind for two months. If there are mouth sores, grind the medicine finely and apply to the sores; it will cool the heat and saliva, leading to healing.

Toad Venom Cotton: For treating early symptoms.
Five pieces of toad venom (about the size of a soapberry), one piece each of borax, dragon brain (camphor), and musk (perfume of musk deer). Grind these into a fine powder, dissolve in half a cup of warm water, and mix with half a qian of red cotton. Dip the cotton in the medicinal juice and let it dry. When the medicinal juice is exhausted, cut the cotton into sections. Apply one piece to the affected area; if saliva is produced, expectorate. Repeat three to five times a day, replacing as needed, to achieve healing.[46p]

Huanglian Jiedu Decoction - for treating front symptoms.

  • Huanglian, Huangqin, Huangbo, and Guizhi in equal parts, decoct with water for consumption.

Yangzheng Dan - for treating front symptoms.

  • Grind one tael each of fine cinnabar, sulfur, mercury, and black lead. Use an iron bowl, burn charcoal to melt the lead into juice, add mercury, stir with willow sticks until mixed, then add the powdered cinnabar, stir until it is invisible. Lift it slightly, then add the sulfur powder, stir rapidly until it rises in flames. Sprinkle with vinegar, wait for it to cool, take out and grind into a very fine powder. Boil it with glutinous rice to make pills the size of mung beans. Each dose is seven fen, to be taken with salted water or red date soup; for individuals with deficient middle energy, use ginseng broth for ingestion.

Heixi Dan - for treating front symptoms.

  • Two taels each of black lead and sulfur, melt the lead gradually adding sulfur until it forms sheets; pour onto the ground to release fire toxins, and grind until silent.

Shengma Decoction - for treating mouth ulcers and rotten gums.

  • Half tael each of Shengma, Yuanshen, Huanglian, Huangqin, Gegen, Lingyangjiao powder, Dahuang, Qianghuo, Fangfeng, and chrysanthemum (remove core); two and a half qian each of ginseng, Zhimu, and roasted licorice. Grind together; each dose is three qian, boil in one cup of water until reduced to seven parts, strain, and take warm after meals. If ginseng is unavailable, substitute with burdock seeds.

Bingye Wan - for treating front symptoms.[47p]

　　龙脑少许　黄蘗日干　硼砂研　薄荷叶各等分　右为细末，研匀，生蜜和丸，如龙眼大，每服一丸，津液化下。疮甚者，加脑子研。

A small amount of dragon brain, yellow foetid vine dried, borax ground, and peppermint leaves in equal parts. Grind into a fine powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of longan. Take one pill each time to promote saliva. For severe sores, add ground dragon brain.

Adjust and decrease the Xie Bai San for treating bad breath.

Three qian of mulberry root, two qian of platycodon, twenty-one grains of Schisandra, one and a half qian of wild yam and honey-prepared licorice, seven fen of anemarrhena, five fen each of scutellaria and ophiopogon. Chop these ingredients, boil with two cups of water until reduced to one cup, strain, and take warm, avoiding food for a while. Take twice daily. Avoid alcohol, damp, and spicy hot foods.

Shengxiang Ointment for treating hot and foul breath.

Dried sweet melon seeds, shelled and ground finely, mixed with a little honey to form a paste. After meals, hold in the mouth, or apply to the teeth for better effect. Another method: after rinsing the mouth, dissolve a pill the size of a jujube pit.

Dibugpi Pills for treating lung heat and bad breath, with a gummy mouth, dry tongue, thirst, and frequent urination.

Dibugpi, mulberry root, gardenia fruit, astragalus, and aristolochia in equal parts ground to a fine powder. Mix with licorice paste to form pills the size of fox nuts. Take one pill after meals to dissolve in the mouth.

Jipeili Huangyuan [Zhongjing] for treating intestinal water qi and dryness of the mouth and tongue.

Fangji, pepper eyes, flax, and rhubarb each one liang. Grind these four ingredients into a powder, form honey pills the size of a tung seed, and take one pill before meals, three times a day. If it slightly increases saliva, those feeling thirsty can add half a liang of mirabilite.[48p]

Raw Rehmannia Decoction: Treats spleen heat, leading to chapped and dry lips without moisture.

Recipe for Curing Bad Breath

  • Ingredients:
    • 20 zhu of orange peel
    • 18 zhu of cassia bark
    • 1 tael of magnolia bark
    • 20 jujubes

Usage: Combine these four ingredients. For treatment, take a small spoonful with wine, three times a day. Long-term use will make the body fragrant. It can also be made into jujube meat balls, taking 20 balls the size of a walnut, gradually increasing to 30 balls. Another recipe includes 18 zhu of chuanxiong.

Da Fen Qing Yin - Treats excessive alcohol damp-heat and oral sores.
Poria, Alisma, and Akebia each 6 grams; Zhu Ling, Gardenia (or double the amount), Bitter Orange, and Plantago each 3 grams; 1.5 cups of water, decoct to 80% remaining, take warm away from meals. If internal heat is severe, add Huang Qin, Huang Lian, and Gentian.

Li Yin Jian - Treats liver and gallbladder deficiency with bitter taste in the mouth.
Prepared Rehmannia 9-21 grams; roasted dried ginger 3-9 grams; Angelica 6-21 grams; honey-fried licorice 3-6 grams; 2 cups of water, decoct to 70-80% remaining, take warm; can add cinnamon 3-6 grams.

Wu Jun Zi Jian - Treats previous condition.
Ginseng 6-9 grams; roasted dried ginger 3-9 grams; honey-fried licorice 3 grams; Atractylodes and Poria each 6 grams; 1.5 cups of water, decoct to take.

Bing Yu San - Treats oral ulceration.
Raw Gypsum 30 grams; Moonstone 21 grams; Borneol 1 gram; silkworm 3 grams; grind to a very fine powder, store in a small ceramic jar, can be applied or blown on.

Bing Bai San - Treatsoral ulcer and aphthae.
Human White (bulk) double the amount; a little Borneol; copper green vinegar preparation; bitter almond equal parts; grind to fine powder, apply to affected area; some prepare Huang Lian with honey equal to Human White and add Borneol. Users should apply as needed.[54p]

Gui Pi Yang Rong Decoction (from "Complete Book of Sores") treats chapped lips.
Ingredients: Angelica, Chuanxiong, white peony, raw earth, Poria, Bupleurum, dried tangerine peel, licorice, angelica dahurica, gardenia fruit, platycodon, ophiopogon, astragalus, white atractylodes, siler, coptis, berberine, peony root, anemarrhena, and for women, add zexie, used acupuncture and cyperus.

Cauterization method: Regardless of gold or silver, make into a branding iron, heat until red with mugwort fire, and apply while hot to the affected area. Repeat burning and application up to five or six times a day, as excessive might harm vital energy. Choose a propitious day, avoiding the gods. Afterward, apply medicine to prevent recurrence.

Root removal and medicine application treat the preceding symptoms.

Sheng Ma Decoction
For treating bladder heat, persistent oral ulcers, and throat swelling.
Ingredients:

  • Sheng Ma (Cimicifuga): 4 liang
  • Yuan Shen (Scrophularia): 4 liang
  • White Skin of Rose Root, cleaned of soil: 4 liang
  • She Gan (Belamcanda): 4 liang
  • Da Qing (Woad): 3 liang
  • Huang Bò: 3 liang
  • Honey: 7 he

Directions: Grind the seven ingredients, use 7 sheng of water, boil down to 1 sheng and 5 he, remove dregs, add honey, and simmer for two more boils. Slowly suck and swallow.

For ointment to treat sores in the mouth, throat obstruction, and dry mouth: one liang each of pig fat, white honey, and coptis. Combine these three ingredients, simmer and strain, stirring until well mixed. Take amounts the size of half a jujube, four to five times a day and twice at night.

Another ointment for treating oral ulcers and throat sores caused by heat, preventing liquid from entering: one liang each of angelica, bulbus reed, and cimicifuga, and half a liang of aconite. Chew these four ingredients, using four liang of pig fat. First, simmer to create an ointment; ensure it doesn’t get too hot on the stove. Then, add the other herbs and simmer on low heat until the aconite turns yellow. Strain out the residue, add four liang of white honey, boil once or twice, then let it set in a container until solid. Take pieces the size of an almond and hold in the mouth four to five times a day, swallowing them.[58p]

Mouth Odor Remedy

Ingredients: Cinnamon heart, Licorice, Asarum, Tangerine peel - equal parts of these four ingredients. Grind and sift with wine, take one penny (weight) in a spoon, and it will stop the odor.

Another Prescription: For previous symptoms.

Eight taels of jujube flesh, four taels each of Chuanxiong, Bai Zhi, tangerine peel, and cinnamon heart. Grind these five ingredients into a powder, mix with jujube flesh, and if it is dry, add honey to form pills the size of a soybean. Take ten pills in the morning, hold them in the mouth before and after meals, or swallow them. In seven days, both the mouth and body will emit a pleasant fragrance.

Mouth Odor Transformed to Fragrance Remedy:

Cinnamon heart (or Asarum as noted in “Records of Old and New”), Licorice in equal parts. Grind these two ingredients into a powder. Before sleeping, take a pinch with fingers and ingest with wine; in twenty days, it will smell fragrant.

Mouth Odor Remedy:

Sichuan pepper and cinnamon heart in equal parts. Grind these two ingredients into a powder. Take three finger pinches in wine.

Removing Odor and Enhancing Fragrance:

Twenty zhu of Licorice, eighteen zhu of Bai Zhi, twenty-four zhu of Chuanxiong. Grind and sift these three ingredients; take a spoonful with wine three times a day for thirty days, and it will smell fragrant.

Another Prescription:

Large jujube, melon seed kernels, and white bark of pine root - grind and sift these three ingredients; take a spoonful with wine two times a day for a hundred days, and all your clothes will smell fragrant.

Another Prescription:

Melon seed kernels, Chuanxiong, dried root, Angelica, Du Huang - six zhu each, half a tael of Asarum, and two taels of Fang Feng. Grind and sift these seven ingredients; take a spoonful after meals three times a day. One formula adds eighteen zhu of Bai Zhi.[60p]

The foul odor from the seven orifices is all overcome by the fragrant formula.

Use: 5 taels of agarwood, 3 taels of the gourd root, half a sheng of white melon seeds, 2 taels each of raw licorice, angelica, and Cyperus rotundus, 2 taels of musk, and 5 he of cloves. 　　口疮，黄蘗酢渍，含之亦愈。 【《本草》，下同】
　　心脾热，口颊舌上生疮：蜜炙黄蘗与青黛为末，掺之差。
　　口舌生疮：溺桶垽七分，枯矾三分，研匀掺之，有涎拭去，数次即愈。[69p]

Rosa canina roots cure mouth sores that have persisted for a long time. Boil them to make a concentrated juice, then gargle with it, warming it in the mouth before spitting it out. It works immediately. Use the roots in winter and the stems and leaves in summer.

To treat bad breath with hair ash, use one qian of hair ash mixed with well water and take it on an empty stomach.

For mouth sores, soak Berberine in vinegar and suck on it for healing.

Mouth sores that are ulcerated and white: use areca nut ash, mix in a small amount of fine powder, and apply it dry.

　　口肥疮：熬灶上饭令焦，末敷之。

　　燕吻疮：木履尾，内煻灰中令热，取拄两吻各二七遍，推之则复入矣。推当疾出其指，恐误啮伤人指也。　　又方：消蜡和水敷之善。

　　卒口噤不开：附子捣末，内管中，强开口，吹口中。
　　口干：羊脂或猪脂，鸡子大劈之，内半升酢中，渍一宿，绞取汁，含之。　　又方：石膏五合，碎，蜜二升。先以水三升，煮石膏取二升，内蜜，煮取二升，去滓含如枣核大，咽汁尽，更含之。
　　虚劳口干：麦冬一两为末，大枣肉三十枚。以蜜一升和令熟，用米五升蒸之，任性服。　　又方：羊脂如鸡子大，醇酒半升，枣七枚，劈合渍七日，取枣食之，立愈。

Mouth Ulcers: Boil rice until scorched and apply the residue.

Another prescription: five offerings of gypsum, crushed, and two liters of honey. First, boil three liters of water with gypsum to extract two liters, then add honey, boil it down to two liters, strain it, and hold it in mouth like a jujube pit until the juice is exhausted, then hold it again.

Dry Mouth from Deficiency: One tael of Ophiopogon powder, thirty pieces of jujube meat. Mix with one liter of honey and cook until thick; steam with five liters of rice and consume at will. Another recipe: chick-sized piece of sheep fat, half a liter of strong wine, seven jujubes, chop and soak for seven days, eat the jujubes for immediate relief.

Foul Breath: Regularly at dawn before the sun rises, walk seven steps from the east wall, turn back towards the wall, and hold water while spitting against it seven times; the mouth will then smell fragrant. Another prescription: hold in your mouth the powders of Asarum and cardamom, which are very effective.[71p]

　　　　　针灸

　　《素问》云：帝曰：有病口苦，取阳陵泉。口苦者病名为何？何以得之？岐伯曰：病名曰胆瘅。夫肝者中之将也。取决于胆，咽为之使。此人者数谋虑不决。故胆虚气上溢，而口为之苦。治之以胆募俞。　　嗌干，口中热如胶，取足少阴。
　　《灵枢经》曰：热病先身濇，倚而热，烦悗，干唇口嗌，取之皮，以第一针五十九。肤胀口干寒汗出，索脉于心不得，索之水。水者肾也。　　《甲乙经》曰：舌下肿难以言，舌纵涎出，廉泉主之。　　口僻，偏历主之。
　　口不能水浆，喎僻，水沟主之。
　　瘈瘲口沫出，上关主之。
　　口僻噤，外关主之。
　　痱痿，臂腕不用，唇吻不收，合谷主之。　　风从头至足，面目赤口痛嚙舌，解溪主之。　　厥，口僻失欠，下牙痛，颊肿恶寒，口不收，舌不能言，不得嚼，大迎主之。　　口僻不正失欠，口不开，翳风主之。　　口僻，刺太渊，引而下之。[72p]

Acupuncture

The "Suwen" states: The Emperor asked: If someone suffers from a bitter mouth, one should use Yanglingquan. What is the name of this disease? How is it caused? Qibo replied: It is called "dampness of the gallbladder." The liver is the strategist within the body. It depends on the gallbladder, and the throat serves as its conduit. Such a person often contemplates but cannot resolve decisions. Hence, the gallbladder is weak, causing qi to overflow upward, resulting in a bitter mouth. Treat it with gallbladder acupoint GB34.

For a dry throat and a hot feeling in the mouth like glue, one should use the foot little yin point. The "Lingshu Classic" states: In febrile diseases, the body first becomes dry, feels hot, and has vexation; with dry lips and mouth, use the skin, applying the first needle at the point number fifty-nine. If there is skin swelling, dry mouth, cold sweat, and the pulse at the heart cannot be felt, examine the kidneys.

The "Jia Yi Classic" states: If the sublingual area swells, making it difficult to speak, and saliva flows excessively, the point Ren 23 should be used. For inability to retain liquids, and with deviations, the point Ren 24 should be used.

Foaming at the mouth and convulsions can be treated with the point SI 3. If there is deviation and difficulty in closing the mouth, use the point SJ 5. For paralysis, incapacitated arms and wrists, and inability to close the lips, use the point LI 4. If wind travels from head to foot causing facial redness, mouth pain, and biting of the tongue, use the point LI 4.

In syncope, with deviation and loss of consciousness, pain in the lower teeth, cheek swelling, chills, inability to close the mouth, and the tongue unable to speak or chew, use the point ST 9. If there is deviation and a lack of consciousness, inability to open the mouth, use the point GB 20. For deviation of the mouth, needle Taiyuan (LU 9) and draw downward.[72p]

　　地仓、大迎，主口缓不收，不能言。　　下关、大迎、翳风，主口失欠，下牙齿痛。　　胆腧、商阳、小肠腧，主口舌干，食饮不下。　　劳宫、少泽，三间、太冲，主口热、口干、口中烂。　　劳宫，主大人小儿口中腥。[73p]

　　　　导引

　　《东垣十书》曰：凡口疮无问新久，夜卧将自己两丸，以手左右交揉，三五十遍，睡觉行之，三五度便差。　　《保生秘要》曰：口干导引法，左右足心每搓三十六回，按时吐纳，津回即咽，六度数过为法，兼后功行之。　　运功以舌抵上腭凝铉雍穴，贯一窟凉水，渐提至口潠咽。　　又法：起涌泉水或肾水皆可。
　　又法：想喉下一窟凉水，以意提起口中，或舌顶上腭，或舌压下腭，则津液自生，或升肾水，或升涌泉水。　　上膈热口干燥，心头推开，又想肾水升至背流出心头洗之，不嘻而吸之，或念背舌托上腭而津液自生。口不能言，先推开肺经，连肾水洗其心肺，又推其舌肋，肺如华盖，覆于心头，不能言者，是火旺肺枯，非肾水不能润之。　　口生蝶毒，清肺经舌托上腭，想水遍舌洗之，次呵出心火。[75p]

Guiding Techniques

The "Ten Books of Dongyuan" states: For any mouth sores, regardless of whether they are new or old, at night sleep with two pills and massage them gently with your hands back and forth 30 to 50 times. When sleeping, do this several times, and it will be alleviated.

The "Essentials for Preserving Life" states: For dry mouth guiding techniques, rub the soles of both feet 36 times, and synchronize with breathing. When saliva returns, swallow it. This should be practiced six times, along with subsequent exercises. Use your tongue to press against the palate at the Yongchuan point, allowing a flow of cool water, gradually lifting it to your throat.

Another method: Visualize a pool of cool water beneath your throat and mentally lift it into your mouth. You may either press your tongue against the palate or the underside of the palate, allowing saliva to form, or raise either kidney water or Yongchuan water.

If there is heat in the diaphragm causing a dry mouth, push it open at the heart level, visualize kidney water rising to cleanse the heart area without making a sound; or think of the back tongue pressing against the palate, and saliva will naturally form. If you cannot speak, first open the lung meridian, connect the kidney water to wash the heart and lungs, then press on the side of the tongue, allowing the lungs to act like a canopy over the heart. If unable to speak, it is due to an overactive fire causing the lungs to dry out; only kidney water can moisten them.

For tongue poisoning, clear the lung meridian by pressing the tongue against the palate and visualize water washing over the tongue, then exhale the heart's fire.[75p]

　　　　医案

　　《儒门事亲》曰：一男子病口疮数年，上至口，中至咽嗌，下至胃脘皆痛，不敢食热物，一涌、一泄、一汗，即去其九，次服黄连解毒，不十余日皆释。
　　赵平尚家一男子，年二十余岁，病口中气出，臭如发厕，虽亲戚莫肯与对语。戴人曰：肺金本主腥，金为火所炼，火主焦臭，故如是也。久则成腐，腐者肾也，此极热则反兼水化也。病在上宜涌之，先以茶调散涌而去其七分，夜用舟车丸、浚川散下五七行，比旦而臭断。呜呼！人有病口臭而终其老者，世讹以为肺系偏而与胃相通，故臭。此妄论也。[76p]

Medical Case

The "Confucian Family Guidelines" states: A man has been suffering from mouth sores for several years, experiencing pain in his mouth, throat, and stomach. He dares not eat hot food; every time he vomits, has diarrhea, or sweats, he feels weakened. After taking Huanglian Jiedu (a herbal remedy), he began to recover in less than ten days.

Zhao Ping’s family had a man in his twenties suffering from an extremely foul odor coming from his mouth, so much so that relatives would not speak to him. An expert said: “The Metal element of the lungs is responsible for odors, and when Metal is refined by Fire, it leads to a burnt, foul smell. Over time, this can result in decay, which pertains to the Kidneys. When this heat is extreme, it also affects the water metabolism. The disease is in the upper part of the body and should be treated with emetics. First, a tea should be used to prepare to induce vomiting and release seventy percent of the condition. At night, take Zhouche Pills and Jun Chuan Powder to move the bowels five to seven times, and by morning, the foul odor will cease. Alas! Those who suffer from bad breath throughout their lives are mistakenly thought to have a connection between the lungs and stomach, resulting in the odor. This is a fallacious theory.”[76p]

　　《卫生宝鉴》曰：梁济民膏粱多饮，因劳心过度，肺金有伤，以致气出腥臭，涕唾稠粘，咽嗌不利，口苦干燥，以加减泻白散主之。《难经》云：心主五臭，入肺为腥臭，此其一也。因洪饮大热之气所伤，使心火刑于肺金，以桑白皮，地骨皮苦微寒，降肺中伏火，而补气为君，以黄芩知母苦寒，治气腥臭，清利肺气为臣肺欲收，急食酸以收之，五味子酸温以收肺气；麦门冬苦寒，治涕唾稠粘，口苦干燥为佐。桔梗辛温，体轻浮，治痰逆利咽膈为使也。
　　《薛己医案》曰：州守刘克新患茧唇，时出血水，内热口干，吐痰体瘦，肾虚之证悉具，用济阴地黄丸年许而愈。
　　一儒者因劳役感暑，唇生疮，或用四物加黄蘗、知母之类而愈。后复作，彼仍用前药，益甚，腹中阴冷。余用补中益气汤加茯苓、半夏，治之而愈。[77p]

The "Hygiene Treasure" states: Liang Jimin, who indulged in rich food and excessive drinking, suffered from overthinking, causing harm to the lung's metal, resulting in foul breath, thick and sticky mucus, discomfort in the throat, and a bitter, dry mouth. This calls for the prescription of the modified Xie Bai San. The "Nanjing" states: the heart governs the five odors, and when entering the lungs, it results in a fishy scent, which is one aspect of it. This is due to the damage caused by excessive heat from consuming large amounts of fluid, which results in heart fire burning the lung metal. Therefore, mulberry bark and earth bone bark, which are slightly bitter and cool, are used to suppress the lurking fire in the lungs, while supplements for Qi are considered primary. Huang Qin and Zhi Mu, which are bitter and cold, treat the fishy odor and clear lung Qi, becoming secondary in function. To help the lungs consolidate, sour foods should be consumed to draw it in, while Shí Wèi Zi, being sour and warm, also helps to consolidate lung Qi. Mai Men Dong, being bitter and cold, treats thick and sticky mucus and a dry, bitter mouth, serving as an assistant. Jie Geng, which is acrid and warm but light and floating, treats phlegm rebellion and benefits the throat.

The "Xue Ji Medical Case" states: The prefect Liu Kexin suffered from chapped lips that occasionally bled, accompanied by internal heat, dry mouth, and thinness, showing signs of kidney deficiency. After using Ji Yin Di Huang Wan for about a year, he recovered.

A Confucian scholar, who fell ill from labor in the heat, developed sores on his lips. Some used Si Wu decoction with Huang Lian and Zhi Mu and recovered. However, the condition recurred, and the same medicine was used again, worsening the symptoms with a cold sensation in the abdomen. I then prescribed Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang with additional Fu Ling and Ban Xia, which successfully treated him.[77p]

　　儒者杨国华因怒，唇口两耳肿痛，寒热。余谓怒生热，热生风，用柴胡山栀散，数剂而愈。
　　一男子素善怒，唇肿胀，服清胃等药时出血水，形体骨立。余用补中益气加半夏、茯苓、桔梗，月余唇肿渐消，元气渐复。又以四物加柴胡、炒山栀、丹皮、升麻、甘草数剂。乃去山栀、加参朮而痊。
　　一妇人怀抱久郁，患茧唇。杂用消食降火，虚证悉具，盗汗如雨，此气血虚而有热也。用当归六黄汤，内黄芩、连、蘗炒黑，二剂而盗汗顿止。乃用归脾汤八珍散兼服，元气渐复。更以逍遥散归脾汤，间服百余剂，而唇亦瘥。
　　一妇人怀抱久郁，或时胃口嘈辣，胸膈不利，月水不调，形衰食少，日晡发热，食少体倦，唇肿年余矣。余用归脾汤加姜汁炒黄连、山栀，少佐吴茱萸，嘈辣顿去，饮食少进。乃去黄连加贝母、远志，胸膈通利，饮食如常。又用加味逍遥散归脾汤，间服百余剂，月水调而唇方痊。[78p]

Confucian scholar Yang Guohua became swollen and painful in the lips and ears due to anger, experiencing chills and fever. I diagnosed the anger as generating heat, which in turn produced wind, and treated him with Chaihu and Shan Zhi powder. After several doses, he recovered.

A man who was prone to anger suffered from swollen lips and, when taking digestive and anti-fire medications, experienced bleeding. He was thin and emaciated. I prescribed a restorative formula (Buzhong Yiqi Tang) with Banxia, Fuling, and Jiegeng added. After a month, the swelling gradually subsided, and his vitality improved. I then adjusted the formula with Siwu decoction, adding Chaihu, fried Shan Zhi, Danpi, Shengma, and licorice in several doses. Finally, I removed the Shan Zhi and added Ren Shen and Bai Zhu, leading to his recovery.

A woman who was emotionally repressed for a long time developed chapped lips. She had mixed treatments that dispelled food and reduced fire, but all signs of deficiency were evident, and she experienced profuse sweating like rain, a condition of Qi and blood deficiency combined with heat. I prescribed the Danggui Liu Huang Decoction, incorporating Huangqin, Lian, and banxiao, cooked black; after two doses, her sweating abruptly stopped. I then gave her Gui Pi Tang and Ba Zhen San together for a gradual recovery of her vitality. Further, I alternated with Xiao Yao San and Gui Pi Tang, taking over a hundred doses until her lips healed.

Another woman, also emotionally troubled for a long time, sometimes experienced stomach discomfort, chest congestion, irregular menstrual cycles, diminished strength and appetite, daily fevers, weariness, and had swollen lips for over a year. I prescribed Gui Pi Tang with fried Huanglian, Shan Zhi added along with a touch of Wuzhuyu; the discomfort and bloating quickly disappeared, but her intake was still low. Then I removed Huanglian and added Beimu and Yuan Zhi, which alleviated her chest congestion, allowing her to eat normally. I further adjusted with an improved version of Xiao Yao San and Gui Pi Tang, alternating over a hundred doses, and after a month her menstrual cycle normalized, and her lips finally healed.[78p]

　　一妇人唇裂内热二年矣，每作，服寒凉之剂，时出血水，益增他证。余用加味清胃散而痊。后因怒，唇口肿胀，寒热而呕。用小柴胡加山栀、茯苓、桔梗，诸证顿愈。复用加味逍遥散而康。
　　一妇人善怒，下唇微肿，内热体倦。用化痰药，食少作呕，大便不实，唇出血水。用理气消导胸膈痞满，头目不清，唇肿经闭。用清胃行血，肢体愈倦，发热烦躁，涎水涌出。余曰：此七情损伤肝脾，误行攻伐所致。遂用济生归脾汤食进便实。用加味逍遥散肿消热退。用补中益气汤，脾健涎止。后因怒，寒热耳痛，胸膈胀闷，唇掀肿甚，此怒动肝火而伤阴血，用四物合小柴胡加山栀顿愈。又因怒，胁乳作胀，肚腹作痛，呕吐酸涎，饮食不入，小水不利，此怒动肝木而克脾土，用补中益气加川芎芍药而愈。又劳役怒气，饮食失节，发热而喘，体倦不食，下血如崩，唇肿炽甚，此肝经有火不能藏血，脾经气虚，不能摄血，用补中益气汤，加炒黑山栀、芍药、丹皮而愈。[79p]

A woman suffered from a cleft lip and internal heat for two years. Whenever symptoms arose, she took cold and cooling medicines, which caused bleeding and worsened her other symptoms. I treated her with an upgraded version of the Qingwei Powder, and she recovered. Later, after an outburst of anger, her lips swelled, accompanied by cold and heat, and vomiting occurred. I prescribed Xiao Chai Hu Decoction with gardenia fruit, poria, and platycodon, and all her symptoms quickly improved. I then used an enhanced version of the Xiaoyao Powder, resulting in her full recovery.

Another woman, prone to anger, had slight swelling of her lower lip and experienced internal heat and fatigue. I gave her phlegm-dissolving medicine, but she had a reduced appetite, experienced vomiting, and had ineffective bowel movements, with bleeding from her lips. I treated her to regulate qi and eliminate chest stagnation, but she still had dizziness, lip swelling, and irregular menstruation. I then used Qingwei to move blood, which eased her fatigue, reduced fever and restlessness, and caused excessive salivation. I noted that her emotional distress had harmed her liver and spleen, yielding wrong treatment through attack. Therefore, I prescribed Jisheng Guipi Decoction to improve appetite and bowel movements, followed by an enhanced Xiaoyao Powder to relieve swelling and reduce heat. I then used Zhongyi Yiqi Decoction to strengthen her spleen and stop salivation.

Subsequently, due to another angry episode, she developed chills, ear pain, chest fullness, and severe lip swelling, suggesting her anger had ignited liver fire, damaging yin and blood. I prescribed the Four Substances Decoction combined with Xiao Chai Hu Decoction and added gardenia fruit, which quickly alleviated her condition. After another fit of anger, her hypochondriac area and breasts felt swollen, her abdomen hurt, and she had sour vomiting, with no intake of food and difficulty urinating. This indicated anger affecting the liver wood, disrupting the spleen earth. I treated her with Zhongyi Yiqi Decoction, adding chuanxiong and peony, which led to her recovery. However, from overexertion and anger, her appetite waned, she experienced fever and shortness of breath, felt fatigued, had severe blood loss akin to a collapse, and pronounced lip swelling. This reflected liver heat unable to retain blood, and spleen qi deficiency unable to contain blood. I treated her with Zhongyi Yiqi Decoction, enhanced with roasted black gardenia, peony, and moutan, leading to her recovery.[79p]

　　一男子内热作渴，咳唾痰涎，大便干濇，自喜壮实，问治于余。余曰：此脾肾阴亏阳旺之证，当壮水之主。不信，自服二陈芩连之类，次年下唇渐肿，小便赤濇。执守前药，唇出血水，大便黑块，小便淋沥。请余往治。余曰：大便结黑，小便淋沥，肝肾败也。唇口肿白，脾气败也。辞不赴，竟殁。
　　一妇人月经不调，两足发热，年余后而身亦热，劳则足腿酸痛，又年余唇肿裂痛，又半年唇裂出血，形体瘦倦，饮食无味，月水不通，唇下肿如黑枣。余曰：此肝脾血虚火证，彼不信，用通经等药而死。[80p]

A man experienced internal heat leading to thirst, coughing up phlegm, and had hard and dry bowel movements. He was pleased with his strong physique and sought treatment from me. I said: This is a condition of kidney and spleen yin deficiency with excess yang; you need to strengthen the water element. Disbelieving, he took herbs like Erchen and Qinian instead. The next year, his lower lip gradually swelled, and his urination became red and painful. Clinging to the previous medication, his lips bled, his bowel movements became black and blocky, and his urination was dribbling. He asked me to treat him. I said: The black dry stool and dribbling urination indicate liver and kidney failure. The swelling and whiteness of the lips signify spleen deficiency. He refused further treatment and eventually passed away.

A woman had irregular menstruation and hot feet. After a year, her body felt hot, and when tired, her legs ached. After another year, her lips swelled, cracked, and hurt. After another six months, her lips bled from the cracks, her body grew thin and fatigued, her appetite diminished, menstruation was obstructed, and her lower lip swelled like a black jujube. I said: This is a condition of liver and spleen blood deficiency with heat. She disbelieved me, took herbs for regulating menstruation, and died.[80p]

　　一妇人善怒，唇肿，或用消毒之药，唇胀出血年余矣。余曰：须养脾胃滋化源方可愈，彼用前药，状如翻花瘤而死。
　　一男子口糜烂，脉数无力。此血虚而有火，用四物加茯苓、白朮，少用黄蘗、知母治之而愈。
　　地官李孟卿子新婚，口舌糜烂，日晡益甚。用八珍汤加五味、麦门冬而口疮愈，更用加减八味丸而元气实。
　　一男子唇舌生疮，口苦作呕，小便淋濇。此肝脾火动，以小柴胡加山栀、酸枣仁、远志、麦门冬，诸证渐愈。但晡热体倦，用四物柴胡、山栀而愈，又加白朮、茯苓、炙甘草而安。
　　一妇人每怒，则口苦兼辣，头痛胁胀，乳内刺痛。此肝肺之火。用小柴胡加山栀、青皮、芎、归、桑皮而安。后劳兼怒，口复苦，经水顿至，用四物加炒山栀、炒胆草一剂，更以加味逍遥散而康。[81p]

A woman is prone to anger, her lips are swollen, and she has been bleeding from them for over a year after using a disinfectant. I said: She needs to nourish her spleen and stomach to restore her digestive source; otherwise, her condition will only worsen like a fatal tumor.

A man has mouth ulcers and a rapid, weak pulse. This is due to blood deficiency combined with heat. I prescribed the Four Substance Decoction with poria and white atractylodes, adding a little yellow berries and anemarrhena to treat him, and he recovered.

However, he still experiences afternoon heat and fatigue; I used the Four Substance with Chai Hu and gardenia, and he improved, further adjusting with white atractylodes, poria, and honey-fried licorice for stability.

A woman experiences bitter and spicy tastes in her mouth when angry, along with headaches and rib distension, and sharp pain in her breasts. This indicates heat in the liver and lungs. I prescribed Xiao Chai Hu augmented with gardenia, citrus peel, angelica, and mulberry bark for relief. Later, after exertion and anger, her mouth became bitter again, and menstruation suddenly began. 　　秋官赵君言口舌生疮，劳则体倦，发热，恶寒。此内伤气血之证，用补中益气加五味麦冬而愈。
　　进士刘华甫口舌生疮，午前热甚，脉数而有力。用清心莲子饮稍愈。更以四物二连汤全愈。后因劳役，日晡发热，脉数而无力，用四物加参、朮、柴胡少瘥。但体倦口干，再用补中益气汤而愈。
　　武库刘君口舌生疮，口干饮汤，乃胃气虚而不能化生津液也，用七味白朮散而痊。
　　廷评曲汝为口内如无皮状，或咽喉作痛，喜热饮食。此中气真寒而外虚热也，用加减八味丸而愈。
　　儒者费怀德发热，口舌状如无皮。用寒凉降火药，面赤发热，作呕少食，痰涎自出。此脾胃复伤虚寒而作也。用附子理中汤以温补脾胃，用八味丸补命门火乃愈。
　　一儒者口苦而辣，此肺肝火证，先以小柴胡加山栀、胆草、茯苓、桑皮而渐愈。更以六君加山栀、芍药而痊。若口苦胁胀，小便淋沥。此亦肝经之病，用六味丸以滋化源。[82p]

In autumn, Master Zhao of the officials reported sores in the mouth, fatigue from exertion, fever, and aversion to cold. This is a sign of internal injury to the qi and blood; treating it with Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction plus Five-Flavor and Mai Dong resulted in recovery.

　　一男子口臭，牙龈赤烂，腿膝痿软，或用黄蘗等药，益甚。时或口咸，此肾经虚热，余用六味丸悉瘥。
　　一妇人口苦胁胀，用小柴胡、山栀、黄连少愈。更以四君子加芍药、当归、柴胡而瘥。
　　一妇人每怒，口苦发热，晡甚，以小柴胡合四物二剂。更以四物加柴胡、白朮、茯苓、丹皮而愈。
　　《医学纲目》曰：宣文炳口流涎不止，喜笑舌喑，脉洪大。用连、芩、蘗、栀、白朮、半夏竹沥、姜汁服之，五日涎止笑息。
　　《证治准绳》曰：常熟严文靖公年逾七十，未断房室。日服温补之药无算。兼以人参煮粥，苁蓉作羹，致滋胃热，满口糜烂，牙齿动摇，口气臭秽，殆不可近。屡进寒凉清胃之药，不效。有欲用姜桂反佐者。请决于予。予曰：用之必大剧。主用加减甘露饮八剂而平。
[83p]

A man has bad breath, his gums are inflamed and rotten, and his knees are weak and soft. Medications such as Huangbo may aggravate the condition. Occasionally, he experiences a salty taste in his mouth, indicating deficient heat in the kidney meridian; using Liuwei Dihuang Wan can cure it completely.

A woman suffers from a bitter taste in her mouth and a distended side. Treatment with Xiao Chaihu, Shan Zhi, and Huang Lian results in slight improvement. Further treatment with Sijunzi Tang, adding Shaoyao and Danggui, leads to recovery.

Another woman, whenever she gets angry, experiences bitterness in her mouth and a feeling of heat, especially in the evening. Treatment with Xiao Chaihu combined with Sihua results in two doses. Subsequent treatment with Sihua plus Chaihu, Baizhu, Fuling, and Danpi brings about recovery.

The "Medical Essentials" states that Xuanwen Bing has incessant drooling, enjoys laughing, and has a dull pulse. Using Lian, Qin, Bo, Zhi, Baizhu, Banxia, bamboo juice, and ginger juice results in the cessation of drooling and laughter within five days.

The "Principles of Diagnosis and Treatment" mentions that Yan Wen Jing, aged over seventy, has not ceased sexual relations. He daily consumes countless warming and nourishing medicines. Additionally, he makes congee with ginseng and soup with Cistanchus, leading to hot stomach, oral ulcers, loose teeth, and foul breath, making it nearly unbearable to approach him. Multiple attempts to use cold, cooling medicines for the stomach have been ineffective. There is a desire to use ginger and cinnamon as adjuncts. Please provide a resolution. I say: Using them will definitely result in serious issues. The main treatment should be an adjusted version of Ganlu Drink in eight doses to restore balance.[83p]
